  निज...रूपस्य— निजमहोत्सवस्य अभ्युदयः, तस्य दर्शनाय प्रतिपन्नं रूपं येन तस्य— 'Who assumed (प्रतिपन्न) & human form to see the glory (अभ्युदय) of his own festival'. माधव was, as it were, the god of Love incarnate, come down to observe his festival.विवि...रामं— विविधैः विभ्रमैः अभिरामं (अवलोकनसुखं)— Delightful with the various graceful movements (विभ्रम).अनु...रम्भं— अनुरूपः अनुरागस्य अनुबन्धः तेन महार्घीकृतः यौवनारम्भः यस्मिन् तत्— The beginning period of youth in which was rendered highly precious (महार्घीकृत) by the worthy unimpeded passion अन्यो...हलं— अन्योन्यदृष्टीनां विनिपाते या वञ्चना, तस्याः अवसरे विद्यमानं यत् चित्तं तेन त्वरमाणं कौतूहलं यस्मिन् तत् (सुखं)—In which their curiosity was aggravated by their hearts disappointed (खिद्यमान) at the time of the failure (वञ्चना to meet the glances of each other. समु... सुन्दरं— समुल्लसितौ साध्वसस्तम्भौ, ताभ्यां मन्थराः अवयवाः तेषु प्रतिलग्नाः स्वेः पुलकः उत्कम्पः च तैः सुन्दरं (सुखं)— (सुखं)— Charming by the sweat, horripilation and tremor produced in (lit. adhering to— प्रतिलग्न) the limbs grown languid through the rising fear (साध्वस) and numbness. साध्वस is fear or nervousness सवि... दारुणं— सविशेषः दुःसहः आयासः, तेन विजृम्भमाणः उद्दामा देहदाहः तेन दारुणं(परिणामं)— on account of the excessive (उद्दामा lit, bodily fever augnented (विजृम्भमाण) by a still more unbearable feeling of exhaustion (आयास) दशापरिणामः—A change of condition. मुहू...दया— मुहर्तमात्रं सम्प्राप्तः पूर्णचन्द्रोदयः यया सा— (Like & young lotus-plant) which could enjoy the full moon's rise only for some time.The lotus-plant withers away because the moon has vanished from sight, after just a moment's glimpse. The ,Terrible unrestrained) same is the case with मालती, who enjoyed the pleasure of his sight for a momant, only to suffer from it.

  मुहूर्त...गमा— मुहूर्तमात्रं हृदयविनिहितः निर्मीयमाणः वल्लभसमागमः यस्याः— Who enjoy for a moment union with her lord, placed (विनिहित) in the heart, being created (निर्मीयमाण) (by the mind or in imagination). निर्भ...माना— निर्भरेण सलिलासारेण सिच्यमाना— (like the earth— मेदिनी), being sprinkled over by a heavy (निर्भर) shower of rain water. शीतलायते— Gets cooled प्रस्फु...शोभितं (मुखपुण्डरीकं)— प्रस्फुरितौ कान्तौ दशनच्छदौ, ताभ्याम् उच्छलन्ती दन्तमुक्तिकावलिः तस्याः कान्त्या सविशेषं शोभितं— 'Rendered peculiarly charming by the lustre of the row of pearl-like teeth shining forth (उच्छलन्ती) from her lovely throbbing lips.' The throbbing of the lips is indicated as an after-effect of love's enjoyment. निर...स्तबकं— निरन्तरम् उल्लसितः पुलकः, तेन पक्ष्मलौ कान्तौ कपोलौ, तयोः घूर्णमानः सन्ततः आनन्दबाष्पाणां स्तचकः यस्मिन् तद् (मुख॰)— On which (is observed) a cluster (स्तबक) of the tears of joy rolling (घूर्णमान) continuously on the cheeks downy (पक्ष्मल) with the rising horripilation. ईष...त्पलं— ईषद्विकसिते निष्पन्दे मन्दे च तारे ययोः, तादृशे उत्ताने मसृणे मुकुलायमाने च नेत्रे नीलोत्पले इव यस्मिन्— On which the eyes (appearing) like blue lotuses, have their pupils (तारा) slightly dilated, steady and languid, (while they i. e. eyes) are uplifted (उत्तान), gleaming soft (ममृण) and bud-like (i. e. half-closed). उद्भि...मनोहर— उद्भिन्नाः स्वेदजलबिन्दवः तैः सुन्दरं ललाटपट्टे, तदेव नवचन्द्रलेखा, तथा मनोहरं— Lovely with the first crescent of the moon in the form of her broad forehead (ललाटपट्टे) bedewed with the rising drops of perspiration. विद...भावा— विदग्धानां सहचरीणां चित्ते संशयितः कौमारभावः यस्याः सा— The suspicion regarding whose virginity is roused in the minds of her shrewd friends.' Her friends, observing these signs of enjoyment have begun to call in question her virginity ! कथामयं कुमार्यपि विदग्धनायकोपभुक्तेव सम्भोगचिह्नालङ्कृतेत्येवं सन्दिह्यमाना भवति।Com. कुमारस्य भावः कौमारं कौमारमेव भावः। V. L. कुमारीभाव— कुमार्याः भावः।

  उद्दामः...रिणी— उद्दाम्नः शशिनः मयूखानां निकुरुम्बेन चुम्बितः अत एव प्रवृत्तः निस्यन्दः यस्य तादृशः चन्द्रमणिहारः, तं धारयति इति सा— Wearing a necklace (हार) of moon gems that has started oozing, being kissed by the multitude of the rays of full (lit. unchecked) moon. For the expression Cf. बाहुरेन्दवमयूखचुम्बितस्यन्दिचन्द्रमणिहारविभ्रमः। उत्तर॰ I. 34. प्रचुर... शयनीये— प्रचुरेण कर्पूरेण सविशेषशिशिरः यः चन्दनरसः तस्य च्छटासारनिकरेण दन्तुरितं यद् बालकदलीपत्रं, तेन यः संवाहनादिव्यापारः तदर्थं त्वरमाणः सहचरीणां सार्थः तेन विरचिता उपनीता च कमलिनीदलमेव जलाद्री तस्याः शयनीये— On beds formed of lotus-leaves serving as wet-sheets, brought by her friends who are hastening (त्वरमाण) to do the shampooing etc. (संवाहन) (to her) by means of the lotus-leaves which are made rough and uneven (दन्तुरित) by the mass of excellent lumps (छटा) of sandal juice, rendered specially cool by plenty of camphor जलार्द्रा— As the Com. takes it,' & wet cloth or garment' (आर्द्रवस्त्रं; its other sense' a fan wetted with water' may also suit here, in which case it would mean a bed provided with wet fans in the form of lotus-leaves brought and arranged by her friends etc. उन्निद्रा— उद्गता निद्रा यस्याः सा— Sleepless.

 स्वेद...रसा— स्वेदेन प्रसृतौ पादपल्लवौ, ताभ्याम् उद्वान्तः पिण्डालक्तकस्य रसः यस्याः— Whose red lac-dye (पिण्डा... रस) is washed away (lit. vomited— उद्दान्त) from her sprout-like feet dripping with perspiration. The Prakrit पज्झरिद, & Deśi word, should be translated by प्रक्षरित. (Cf. Marathi पाझरणे). Cf. क्षरः खिर—झर—पज्झर—पच्चड णिच्चळ—णिदुआः। हेमचन्द्र— प्राकृत व्याकरण VIII. 4. 173. थर... बन्धना—थरथरायमानं यत् परम् ऊरुमूलं, तेन विसंवदितं नीवीबन्धनं यस्याः सा— The knot of whose garment became loosened by the plump (पीवर) throbbing root of her thighs. Cf. कान्ते तल्पमुपागते विगलिता नीवी स्वयं बन्धनात्। वासो विश्लथमेखलाकरधृतं किञ्चिन्नितम्बे स्थितम्। स्थितम्। अमरु॰ . उत्क्षु... बन्धना— उत्क्षुभ्यतः हृदयान्तरात् (निर्गताः) उत्तरङ्गा निःश्वासाः तैः विषमं (यथा तथा) उच्छ्रसन्तौ पक्ष्मलौ पयोधरा, नयोः उपरि निहिते वेपमाने भुजलते एव वेष्टबन्धनं यया सा— Keeping her throbbing creeper— like arms as a covering (वेष्टबन्धनं) on her thrilled (पक्ष्मल) breasts which violently heave (up and down) by her wave-like sighs from inside the over-excited (उत्क्षुभ्यत्) heart. उत्तरङ्ग— Lit. उदूताः तरङ्गाः यस्मिन्—With waves surging inside. Cf. प्रत्यग्रहीत् पार्थिववाहिनीं तां भागीरथीं शोण इवोत्तरङ्गः। रघु॰ VII. 36. अपामिवाधारमनुत्तरम्। कुमा॰ II 1. 48. पक्ष्मल— Full of horripilation वेष्टनं—उपरिवर्तिप्रियस्य भुजलताबन्धनमालिङ्गनभावनया। Com. झटिति— Suddenly प्रति... लोचना— प्रतिबोधवेलायां विसर्जिताः उद्विग्ना दृष्टिपाताः तैः विज्ञातं यत् शून्यं शयनीयं तेन सञ्जातः मोहः, तस्मात् भीलन्ती लोचने यस्याः सा— Whose eyes would close in a swoon (मोह), to find the bed empty while looking about with stricken (उद्विग्न) glances when suddenly (झटिति) awakened from sleep (प्रतिबोध). प्रियप्राप्त्या प्रबुद्धा \। प्रबोधश्व स्पर्शादिना भवति । ससं... जीविता-संसभ्रमस्य सखीजनस्य प्रयत्नेन प्रतिपन्नः यः मूर्च्छाविच्छेदः, तस्य समये सङ्गलिताः (निःसृतः) ये दीर्घनिःश्वासाः, ते एव शेषजीवितं यस्याः सा—In whose case what remains of life is the long sighs escaping her at the time when the swoon has ended by the effort of her bewildered friends. किङ्कर्तव्यमूढता— 'Being at a loss to know what to do being at one's wit's end. Such is the condition of her friends and not hers. They could not find any means to console her and give her refief in her suffering. प्रथ...सानं— प्रथमं प्रार्थितं निजजीवितस्य अवसानं येन तं— Who eagerly sought the end of their own life. वयमेव प्रथमं प्रियामहे। Com. दुर्वा...पारं दुर्वाराणि देवविलसितानि तेषाम् उपालम्भः एव व्यापार यस्य तं— For whom censuring the irresistible toul play of Fate was the only activity remaining.

 लव... लवेषु— लावण्यं भूयिष्ठं यत्र एतादृशं यद् निर्माणं तेन परिपेलवानि— Delicate because of such a frame (निर्माण) where loveliness predominates दारुणविजृम्भितस्य दारुणं विजृम्भितं यस्य तस्य (मन्मथस्य)— Who has actcd so dreadfully कियच्चिरं... भविष्यति— How long will he go on with happy results? She means, he i. e. Madana cannot continue with his havoc for a long time, for Mālatī will soon break down. कुशलाव सानता— कुशलम् अवसानं, तस्य भावः क्षेमपर्यवसायित्व— The condition of a happy ending (अवसान). रमण... वरणानि— कलहकोपेन यः उपरागः तेन पल्लवितः यः केरलीकपोलः तद्वत् कोमलः उद्वेल्लन् विमलः चन्द्रः तस्य चन्द्रिकया उद्दामलितं तिमिरस्य आवरणं येषा तानि (विभावरीमुखानि)— Whose veil (आवरण) of darkness has been violently (उद्दाम) torn asunder (दलित) by the light of the rising (उद्वेल्लन्) moon, soft and clear like the cheek of a Kerala woman (केरली), kindled (पल्लवित) with the glow of anger in the love-quarrels with her lover (रमण). Kerala women were noted for their beauty. Cf. तस्या अतिगौरत्वेन लोहित्यार्थं ग्रहणम् । Cf. विभावरीमुखानि—The forepart or the opening hours (मुख) of the nights (विभावरी). उल्ल... ङ्गनाः—उल्लसितः यः दुग्धसिन्धोः पूरः तद्वत् धवलम् उज्वलं, च ज्योत्स्नाजलं, तेन प्रक्षालितं गगनाङ्गनं यैः ने (०परिणाहा :)—Which wash the court-yard (अङ्गनं) of heaven with the water of the moon-light, bright and white like the rising flood (tide) of the Milky Ocean (दुग्धसिन्धु) परि...मुखा— परिमलिताः (सञ्जातपरिमलाः) ये पाटलाचकुलाः तेषां निर्मथेनन यः बहल— परिमलस्य उद्गारः, तस्य संवलनेन (मिश्रीभावेण) मसृणाः मांसलायमानाः ये मलयमारुताः तैः उद्भूमाथितानि दशदिशां मुखानि यै— Which render smoky the faces of the ten quarters by means of the gentle **Malaya** breezes, fattened (मांसलायमान) with the mixing (संवलन) of the thick perfume, emitted (उद्वार) on account of their frietion (निर्मथन) with the fragrant पाटला and बकुल flowers. परिमलित is a form like कुवलयित, obtained by the addition of the suffix इतच् to the word परिमल, in the sense of तदस्य सञ्जातम्। वसन्तरजनीपरिणाहाः— The protracted or long-drawn (परिणाह) nights of spring. V. L. ०परिणामाः, which would refer to the closing hours of the nights,' having already spoken about मुखानि.

 III. 14. तद्विषयः— सः (माधवः) विषयः यस्य सः— Which has him as the object. गुणज्ञता— Appreciation of the merits (of माधव) नन्दितं— Delighted, pleased. स्थाने. adv. It is proper, justly. प्रमादः—अनिष्टम्— Calamity.

 III. 15 सौकुमार्यैकसारं— सौकुमार्यमेव एकः सारः स्थिरांशः यत्र तद् (वपुः)— With its one (and only) essence of delicacy. She points out the contrast between the frail delicate body of and the fierece God of Love with his five arrows (पञ्चचाण). Cf. अरविन्दमशोकं च चूतं च नवमल्लिका। नीलोत्पलं च पञ्चैते पञ्चवाणस्य सायकाः। To add to it, has come spring with its fragrant breezes, mango blossoms and lovely moon. चलि... प्रसूनः—चलितैः मलयवातैः उद्भूतानि चूतानां (आम्रवृक्षाणां) प्रसूनानि यस्मिन्— At which the mango-blossoms are stirred by tho blowing Malaya breezes चारु...तंसः— चारुचन्द्रः अवतंसः यम्य— For whom the lovely moon serves as an ear-ornament (अवतंस) सनाथं युक्तं— Possessed of सञ्जीवनं— Life restoring, bringing to life.

 III. 16. परि...वैजयन्ती— परिणतः यः विसकाण्डः, तद्वत् पाण्डुः मुग्धः च यः स्तनपरिणाहः तस्मिन् विलासवैजयन्ती— (The garland which is) a flag (proclaiming) the charms of her full-grown, expansive breasts, pretty and white like a developed lotus-stalk..

Note the poet's self-contradiction, in that, elsewhere he describes her 'budding breasts' (स्तनमुकुल). II. 5.

 कलकलः— A great noise. जानपदाः— Inhabitants of a country(जनपद), as opposed to पौर 'a citizen'. यौव...निवेशः— यौवनारम्भगर्वेण सम्भृतौ दुर्विष अमर्षशेषौ तयोः व्यतिकरेण यः बलात्कारः, तेन विघटितम् उद्घाटितं च यत् लोहपञ्जरं, तत्र निबद्धा शृङ्खला, तस्या निरोधस्य यः प्रतिभङ्गः तेन सङ्कलितः यः निजलीलाविलासः तेन उद्वेल्लन् यः बहलः उजुङगश्च लाङ्गुलः, तस्य विकटेन वैजयन्तिकायाः इव आडम्बरेण उद्यामशरीरसंविनेशः यस्य सः— Whose bodily form (सन्निवेश) is fierce because of the formidable (विकट) banner like lisplay (आडम्बर) of the heavy long tail (लाङ्गूल) uplifted in natural playful grace regained (सङ्कलित) after breaking through (प्रतिभङ्ग) the strong hold (निरोध) of the chain that secured (him) to the iron cage which was burst (विघटित) and flung open (उद्घाटित) in a mingled (व्यतिकर) feeling of intolerance (अमर्ष) and rage, which have become unbearable having been developed .(सम्भृत) by the pride of the prime of youth. मटात्— From the convent. तत्क्षण... कन्दरः— तत्क्षणे सतृष्णं कवलिताः अनेकदेहिदेहाः, तेषा अवयवमध्यगताः निष्ठुराः अस्थिखण्डाः तेषां टङ्कारेण कटकटायमानाः करपत्रवत् कटिनाः दंष्ट्राः, ताभिः करालं मुखकन्दरं यस्य सः— Whose cave-like mouth is horrid with saw-like (करपत्र) harsh jaws creating & grating sound (कटकटायमान) by the cracking (टङ्कार) of hard bits of bones from the limbs of the bodies of many creatures gobbled (रुवलित) hungrily. प्रच... निवहः— प्रचण्डवज्रनिर्घातवद् दारुणः चपेटः, तेन आमोटनं तेन पातिताः अनेकनरतुरङ्गाः, तेषां जाङ्गलं (मांस), तस्य उगारण भरितः— गलगुहागर्भः, तत्र गम्भीरः घर्घरः यः उरल्लिः (गलगर्जितं), तेन यः गल्लपूरणशब्दः, तस्य सन्दर्भेण प्रतिरवाभोगः (प्रतिशब्दविस्तारः), तेन भीषितः नष्टो (यथा भवेत् तथा) विद्रावितः अशेषजननिवहः येन सः— Who frightened and routed out of sight (नट) the whole crowd (निवह) of people by the wide-spreading (आभोग) echo of the continuous sound (सन्दर्भ) of his deep and hoarse mouth-illing (गल्लपूरण) growls (उरल्लि) from the depth of his cave-like throat filled with the eructation (उद्वार) of the flesh (जाङ्गले) of many men and horses levelled down by the smashing blow of a slap from his paw, (which is) as disastrous as the fall of the ponderous thunderbolt. कठोर...पथः— कठोरः नखरश्च कपेरः, तेन आक्रमणं, तेन निर्दयं दारिता जन्तूनां गात्रावयवाः, तेभ्यः प्रवृत्तेन रक्तेन कढ़ीमितः गतिपथः येन सः— Who made his track miry (कर्दमित) by the blood issuing from the limbs of the bodies of animals cruelly mangled, after having been overpowered (आक्रमण) with his hard and sharp (नखर) paw (कर्पर) लीलायितं—The play, sport.

 सहर्षसाध्वसम्— With mingled joy and fear. अम्महे एषोऽपीहस्थ एव। अम्महे— An exclamation of joy and wonder,(almost in the sense of Marathi अगबाई ! ...अगबाई ! हेही इथेञ्च !) अत...लोचनया—अतर्कितं (यथा तथा) उपनतं यद् दर्शनं तेन उल्लसिते लोचने यस्याः सा— Whose eyes brightened at my unexpected (अतर्कित) sight.

 III. 16. He describes his feelings of pleasure and happiness, at being observed by with those eyes of love and joy. पॉण्डरकेिण दाम्ना— By a garland of lotus flowers. पुण्डरीकाणाम् इदं— पौण्डरीकम् अविरलं बद्धः— Closely bound. The bright and white series of glances on him was, as it were, a garland of lotuses. स्नपितः— Bathed निर्भरण दुग्धस्रोतसा— By a thick stream (स्रोतस्) of milk. Her steady gaze is fancied to be the stream of milk which bathes him. कुत्स्नः कवलितः— Entirely or completely swallowed.स्फारितेन—Dilated, expanded. “The eyes in wonder have been so widely dilated that I am completely swallowed by them, as it were! प्रसभं— Forcibly. सान्द्र— Thick. साटोपं— In & majestic way. अप्रमत्तः— Without being negligent, careful, cautious. संशयः— Risk, danger.

 III. 17 संस... खण्डः— संसक्तं त्रुटितं विवर्तिनम् अन्त्रजालं तेन व्याकीर्ण (सद्योहतत्वात्) स्फुरत् अपवृत्तं (अधोमुखं) रुण्डखण्डं (कबन्धरूपं शकलं) यत्र सः (मार्गः)— Having the quivering remains of upturned (अपवृत्त) trunks, and spread over with a net work of entrails, sticking (to. the ground), cut up in pieces, and rolled up in coils (विवर्वित). कीला...पङ्कः— कीलालव्यतिकरेण (रक्तसङ्घेन) गुल्फघ्नः गुल्फपरिमाणः पङ्कः यत्र स— With an ankle-deep mud formed by the mixing of blood (कीलाल). गुल्फदघ्न is a word obtained by the addition of दघ्नन् in the sense of प्रमाण. Cf. प्रमाणे द्वयसज्दघ्नञ्मात्रचः। पा॰ सू॰ V. 2—37.

Cf. ऊरुदन्घ्न, जानुदघ्न etc. गुल्फः प्रमाणमस्य। प्राचण्ड्यं— प्रचण्डस्य भावः— A frightful aspect. नग्वायुधः— A tiger. नखाः आयुधं यस्य।.

  III. 18 क्रमगता— Gone within his reach or clutches .तदभिपातितात् पुरुषात्. From a man felled down by him i. e. the tiger Note how the verse is being recited in bits by the various characters. अन्याहितं—महद्भयं— A great danger or calamity. दुर्जातं— Evil, calamity. व्यालनिवहः— व्यालस्य नखरैः निःसृतः रक्तनिवहः यस्य। क्षिति...ष्टम्भः— क्षितितले निषक्तायाः खङ्गलतायाः अवष्टम्भेग निश्चलः— (Making himself) steady with the support of his creeper-like sword stuck (निषक्ता) into the ground. क्राम्यति.— Faints.

**IV Act.**

  विपन्नजनानुकम्पिन— One who is compassionate (अनुकम्पिन्) for the afflicted (कमण्डलु)— A wooden or earthen water-pot used by ascetics. पटाञ्चलं— The skirt of the garment सखि लवङ्गिके दिष्ट्या etc. intends her speech for माधव, but it would be hardly consistent with the character of a well-bred girl to address herself directly and unreservedly to the man for whom she has conceived a passion, and must on that account make her open advances as slow as possible, especially as she has not been yet given to him by her father. She, therefore, looks at and लवङ्गिका directs her speech to her. एष एव सः— This is he i. e. मकरन्द', whose cause of love बुद्ध॰ was pleading with her, and for whom she had begun to feel some attachment. This is the first time she sees him, although, as the stage direction at the beginning of the Act,— **मदयन्तिका**-लवङ्गिकाभ्याम् अवलम्बितौ...माधव**मकरन्दौ** etc., tells us that she was holding him in his arms! This she does, however, in ignorance of his identity, and out of gratitude for him, her saviour. The other reading for this stage-direction **मालती**मदयन्तिकाभ्याम् अबलम्बितौ which makes to support माधव her lover, would appear to be a better reading, were it not inconsistent with our notions of an Indian girl like मालती, who would not and should not be bold enough to even do the needful service in such situations! अन्यादृशेषु— Persons of a different nature; not so noble as माधव. or मकरन्द— Partial, having a special liking for, and therefore speaking well of them. Com. रमणियः— Sweet, pleasing. She suggests that मालती's selection of her man is also good, and it is all pleasing to hear the talk of their love, although it has reached the stage of a scandal. रमणीयोर्जितं दर्शनं— An interview which is both romantic and striking or glorious (ऊर्जितं) in rousing love in eachother's heart. रमणीयं सम्भ्रमस्त्रस्तांशुकं सम्यग्विभाव्य परस्परावयत्रसौष्ठवग्राहित्वेन साध्वसव्याजाद् दृढालिङ्गनमहोत्सवानुबन्धित्वेन च मनोहरम्। तथा ऊर्जितं बलवद् दुस्तरविपन्त्रिस्तरणोपकारमूलत्वेन। दैवात्— (Brought about) by Fate. It was really goodluck that the two have met eachother in such a nice and romantic situation, which could never have been possibly arranged by us.सन्निधापित— Made to be near or present (on the scene). काचिद् वार्ता— Some news. He hesitates to tell what he has heard about the proposal of giving मालती to नन्दन, lest he should wound her feelings and give her a shock.परातपन्— Hastily returning. शार्दू...गतां— शार्दूलावस्कन्दस्य गोचरगतां— Within the reach of the tiger's attack (अवस्कन्द). विमृसतः—Think, reflect, as to what the news might be. सुहृद्बुद्ध्या वर्धितोऽसि मालती—You havo been congratulated by on your friend's recovery from his swoon (बुद्धि). प्रीतिदायस्य वर्धापकदानस्य— Of a gift as a token of joy or pleasure and also of love. When a good news is told the person who brings the news, deserves to be given a reward.

 IV. 1. व्याल...मुग्धं (मां)— व्यालेन वणितः यः सुहृद्, तस्य प्रमोहेन मुग्धः, त— I) who lost my consciousness at (the sight my friend wounded by the tiger. सौजन्यात्— Out of her gentle gracious nature, out of her goodness (of the heart).मा गन्तव्यथं विहितवती— Made me free of the trouble, removed my pang यत्... तद्— Since...therefore. पूर्णपात्रवृत्त्या— In the nature of or as (वृत्या) a present willingly parted with and given over to a person who brings the happy news. Of.हर्षादुत्सवकाले यदलङ्कारांशुकादिक। **आकृष्य गृह्यते** पूर्णपात्रं स्यात् पूर्णकं च तद्। or वर्धापकं यदानन्दादलङ्कारादिकं पुनः। आकृष्य गृह्येते पूर्णपात्रं पूर्णाीनकं च तद्॥ हारावली. The presents are not in fact gifts, but are snatched away from the person, as by right. therefore means that she can () take away these things viz. my heart and my very life, as her legitimate reward and he would most gladly part with them. Cf. कदा मे तनयजन्ममहोत्सम्वानन्दनिर्भरो हरिष्यति पूर्णपात्रं परिजनः। काद॰ प्रतीष्टः—Accepted, received. परमेश्वरेण— By the king, the Supreme Lord.' सम्भावयामः— Do honour to, celebrate. कारयामः। प्रमोदः— उत्सवपूर्वकः हर्षः।. वैवर्ण्यं— विवर्णस्य भावः— Paleness, loss of colour सहपांसुक्रीडनात्— By having played together (even as children) in the dust (पांसु); being friends from the earliest childhood. युष्माकं लाभेन— By having obtained you (as our nearest relatives). सखि अस्माकं....मन्त्रयितव्यम्— ‘What, oh friend, must this be told even to us?' लवङ्गिका means 'There is no question, whatsoever, that we have gained as much as you have, why even more, by this alliance with the king's favourite, and that therefore there is no need of telling us these obvious things.' Another interpretation would be— Well, we too have to say that our desires have also been fulfilled by this alliance.' यदेतत्त्वया मन्त्रितमस्माकं मनोरथाः पूर्णा युष्माकं लाभेनेति वयमेव तद्वदामः। तेन त्वं मकरन्देन परिणेतव्येति मनोरथा अस्माकमेव पूर्णा भविष्यन्तीति गूढमुक्तम्। व्यक्तं तु युष्माकं राजमित्राणां लाभेन वयमेव पूर्णमनोरथा इति भावः।Com. One more interpretation, suggested by जगद्धर We too have with us & precious possession in Kāmandakī (Pr. मन्तिदव्वं = मन्त्रिद्रव्य)' is far-fetched. हृद... सुन्दरं— हृदयभरित उद्वृत्तौ च विस्मयानन्दौ, ताभ्यां सुन्दरं यथा तथा (पर्यस्यन्ति)— In & manner charming on account of the joy and wonder that remain (उद्वृत्त) after having filled their hearts. The form is explained as भरः सञ्जातोऽस्य। आन्दो... हराः— आन्दोलायमानेन (upset, disturbed, lit swinging)— धीरत्वेन मनोहराः (कटाक्षाः)। Read पर्यस्यन्ते— Are cast or exchanged. The Pr. पल्हत्यन्ति is Passive Pres. III P1. of पल्हत्थ, a Desi form equivalent to Sanskrit पर्यस् 'to throw.' (Comp. Mar. पालथा). Bh. Wrongly takes it as पर्यस्यन्ति, दलि...सदृशाः— दलितं यद् नीलोत्पलं, तत्सदृशाः— Like full-bloomed lotusos मनो...बन्धी— मनोरथैः निर्वृत्तः सम्बन्धः याभ्यां तौ— Who have accomplished their union in their mental yearnings. मानसं मोहनं— Mental enjoyment.

  IV. 2. ईष... विषमं—ईषत् यद् तिर्यग् वलनं, तेन विषमं— Slow and hesitating because slightly turned askance (तिर्यक). कूणितप्रान्तं—With its corners contracted (कूणित). दृष्टिद्वयेन सुरतप्रागवस्थोक्ता। प्रेमो ... लुलिनं— प्रेम्णः उद्भेदात्-अतिपरिपाकात् स्तिमितं लुलितं—अर्ध—मुकुलितं च।Steady and half-closed on account of the development of passion. अनेन रताभोग उक्तः किं...भ्रू— किञ्चिदाकुञ्चिते ध्रुवौ यत्र।अन्तः... मसृणं—अन्तर्मोदस्य अनुभवेनं मसृणं— Softened in the relish of internal joy. अत्र रतावसानमाह।स्तम्भ... पक्ष्म—स्तम्भेन, (कथं पुनः सङ्गमो भावीति) चिन्तया निष्कम्पं पक्ष्म यस्य।आकेकराक्षम् आकेकरं (आकुञ्चितं) अक्षि यत्र— With the eyes contracted or half-closed (आकेकर).

 IV. 3. जीवितप्रदाय— Lit. the giver of my life, Saviour. माधव gives vent to his mood of despair which has filled him at the sad news of the proposed marriage of मालती with नन्दन. बिसि... भिदुरः—बिसिनी— सूत्रवद् भिदुरः भेदनस्वभावः— Liable to break or fragile like a lotus—fibre आशातन्तुः— The thread of hope Evidently he refers to his hopes long cherished, for winning मालती. आधिव्याधिः— आधिर्मनोव्यथा, तद्रूपा व्याधिः— The disease of mental agony निरवधिः— Without any limit, unchecked. पारिप्लवधुरा— चपलकक्षा, चिनचाञ्चल्यस्य अरतिरूपस्य धुरा— The yoke of restlessness. प्रतिष्ठां व्रजतु— स्थितिं बध्नातु— Fix itself, settle down. अव्याजं— निष्कपटं विस्रम्भेण— Undisguisedly, freely. स्वास्थ्यं धत्तां— निराकुलो भवतु— Be at ease. भवतु मदनः— Cf. काम इदानीं सकामो भवतु येनासत्यसन्धे जने सखी पदं कारिता। शा॰ IV.

  IV. 4. समानप्रेमणं—समानं प्रेम यस्य सः तं— The person (i. e. मालती) whose love was equally (intense) वामारम्भे—वामः प्रतिकूलः आरम्भः यस्य— Whose working was opposed to me. परिणतिः— The result, development. For this idea Cf. प्रतिकूलतामुपगते हि विधौ विफलत्वमेति बहुसाधनता। दान... समये. At the tims of hearing (the news) of her being given away (to नन्दन). Her face that turned pale at the shock of the news is likened to the lustreless morning moon.प्रवि... प्रभं— प्रविगलन्ती प्रभा यस्य तद्. Whose lustre was being lost. प्रात... हुति— प्रातन्द्रस्य इव द्युतिः यस्य तद्— Having the lustre of the moon of early morning. Of.... पुनर्दृष्टिं बाष्पप्रसरकलुषामर्पिवती। मयि क्रूरे यत्तत् सविषमित्र शल्यं दहति माम्॥ शा॰ VII. 9.

  दुष्करं प्राणिति— She lives a miserable life. निराशा— With all hope Jost निर्गता आशा यस्याः । अमंस्त— Aorist III sing. of rt. मन् to think. 'भूरिवसु...दास्यति— Hor argument is that since भूरिवसु, मालती's father, never promised माधव or gave him any inkling to imagine that he himself would give her to him, the present news does not alter the situation in the least न परिहीयसे— 'You have not lagged behind (परिहीयसे) the situation in which you were before you heard this news; although I admit, the situation has not improved, you are none the worse off than before'.दत्त...ङ्क्यते— मकरन्द hits at the weak point in her argument मालती before was a free girl and could be wooed by him without any fear or impediment. But now she is दत्तपूर्वा 'Already given to another' by her father, before he could endeavour to secure her for himself. There is thus the fear of the father now, and the obstacle of नन्दन in the way, apart from the moral aspect of cherishing desire for one who is thus given away. स्वयं राज्ञैव— By the King himself and not by भूरिवसु वाक्प्रतिष्ठानि— वाचि प्रतिष्ठा येषां तानि— 'Depending or based upon the words uttered.' व्यवहारतन्त्राणि— Affairs, dealings. She means that the words uttered, by way of giving promises or assurances govern the mutual dealings of men. It is the words that bind men and make them responsible for their actions. Bhūrivasu for instance by his remark, प्रभवति **निजस्य** कन्यका—जनस्य महाराजः, caa any moment turn round and remind people of what he actually said, if at all they would blame himn for his breach of promise. पुण्या... हेतवः व्यवस्थाः— All arrangements resulting in merit or sin. वाचि आयतन्ते— Rest or depend on words. The question of sin is also settled in view of the utterances of the man in his transactions. The truthful धर्मराज too, took advantage of words, when he declared loudly on the battle-field that अश्वत्थामन् was killed', although ending in a bow tone that it was an elephant of this name. Cf. अश्वत्थामा हत इति पृथामृनुना स्वष्टमुक्ते। स्वैरं शेषे गज इति किल व्याहृतं सत्यवाचा॥ वेणी॰ III. प्रमाणम्— Authority. धर्माचारसमयः— An established guiding principle (समय) of religious behaviour, a religious convention.अविमर्शितव्यम्— Not fit to be taken into consideration; should not be thought of. V. L. विमर्शितव्यम् is a matter for thought, has to be considered, (before giving any decision)' since it has no sanction of usage or scriptural authority. Note the very skilful analysis and discussion of the situation with a view to make out (and reaffirm) that the intelligence given by the man makes no difference in the condition of माधव as regards the prospect of getting मालती. For even before, he knew what भूरिवसु had said to the King as regards the giving of मालती to नन्दन, and now we have been told that she has been given by the king. भूरिवसु's words really did not authorise the king to do so; for though they were true in themselves, they were not applicable to मालती . Hence the King's act cannot bind भूरिवसु' Bh. अनवधाना— नास्ति अवधानं यस्याः सा— Inattentive, heedless.

 IV. 5. सपत्नेषु— शत्रुषु— Even in enemies. पापं— Evil, calamity— अतिस्नेहः पापशङ्की। शा॰ IV or प्रेम पश्यति भयान्यपदेऽपि। युज्यमानं— योग्यं, it, proper.

 IV. 6. Construe:— निजे अस्मिन् शिशुजने दया वा स्नेहो वा भवत्याः चित्तं संसाराद् विरतम् अपि द्रवयति। अतश्च प्र....मुखः (अपि) ते यत्नः प्रसक्तः (सन्)— प्रभवति। अपरं (तु) देवं (प्रभवति)। द्रवयति. Melts, softens. प्रव... मुखः— प्रव्रज्यायाः सुलभः यः समयाचारः तस्माद् विमुखः— (Although) running counter or antagonistic to the prescribed course of conduct natural to an ascetic life (प्रव्रज्या). प्रसक्तः प्रभवति— अविच्छिन्नः सन्ः प्रभवति— Being constant or ceaseless prevails i. e. proves effective. Bh. takes it in a different way. 'प्रसक्तः— प्राप्तः सञ्जातप्रसङ्गः— An occasion for thy effort has come to exist or thy exertion has become due'. दैवमपरं (प्रभवति)—But then there is another force viz. Fate which, too prevails and pulls the other way. सकरुणानुरागं— करुणया अनुरागेण च सहितं यथा तथा— With pity and love. कष्टम्— Alas ! एतावती लोकयात्रा— This much career or association (of माधव with मालती).

 IV. 7. प्रकटय्य— प्रकाश्य— Having shown or manifested. एकरसां— एकः रसः यत्र तां— In which there was only one flavour i. c. unalloyed, of one kind, equable. अकाण्ड... दारुणः—अकाण्डाद् अकस्माद् विवर्तनेन— अन्यथा भावेन दारुणः— Cruel in its sudden turn प्रविशिनष्टि (रूजं)— Intensifies, heightens. This verse is repeated in IV act of the उत्तररामचरित. फलं पारणतं— The fruit (of my life of love) has ripened and therefore it marks the close of this life. अत्र पुरा विरहदशायां माधवप्रतिच्छन्दकादिदर्शनाद् धारितस्य जीवितस्य पर्यवसानं वृत्तम्। Com. कापालिकत्वं— His nature as that of a man belonging to the sect, i. e. episode his ruthless and cruel nature. This suggests the of the V Act. निर्व्यूढं— 'Proved true, carried out successfully, indicated.' Cf. हा तात, निर्व्यूढस्तेऽपत्यस्नेहः। उत्तर॰I निर्वाहः प्रतिपन्नवस्तुषु सतामेकं हि गोत्रव्रतम्। मुद्रा॰. प्रतिष्ठितः— Effected, completed, accomplished. दारु...परिणामः— The result or the development suited to his cruel working. Bh.understands प्रतिष्ठित in the sense of ‘ensured, rendered certain, settled'. Fate rendered her passion so strong and unbearable that it made a havoc on her constitution, and now the end is in keeping with this, in as much as she is not to be happy but miserable for ever, and perhaps to die आश्वासनमात्रं— Mere consolation सह...कातरा— सहजस्नेहेन कातरा। संश... फल्यः— संशयितं जन्मसाफल्यं (मालतीप्राप्त्या) यस्य सः—Whose achievement of his life's object is in suspense or hangs in the balance. महामांसविक्रयात्— Other than selling human flesh (महामांस). For its significance, see the Introduction.

 IV. 8. सरसप्रहारं— Whose wounds were fresh or bleeding (सरस) अग... रीया— न गणितं स्वलद् उत्तरीयं स्तनावरणवासः यया सा। Unmindful of the upper garment slipping down एतेन निरन्तरस्तनस्पर्शः सूचितः। त्रस्तै... दृष्टिः स्तः एकहायनः (एकं हायनं वर्षं यस्य) कुरङ्गः तस्य इव विलोला दृष्टिर्यस्याः सा—Having unsteady eyes like those of a one-year old fawn. The phrase is repeated in the उत्तर॰ III. अमृतसंवलितैः— Besmeared with nectar. 'बुद्धरक्षितप्रियसखी must be taken as a हेतुगर्भ विशेषण, 'easy to be got because she is the friend of बुद्ध॰ who will influence her in your favour and induce her to marry you.' Bh.

 IV. 9. क्रव्याद or द्— A carnivorous animal like a tiger.व्यक्त...रमणीयः व्यक्तेन स्नेहेन स्तिमितः रमणीयश्च— Steady and charming through mainfcsted love पारासिन्धुसम्भेदः— पारा च सिन्धुश्च ते नद्यौ तयोः सम्भेदः सङ्गमः— The confluence of the rivers पारा and सिन्धु. For its location, see Introduction अवगाह्य— Having bathed.

  IV. 10. Constrne :— स्नानमात्रोत्थिताभिः जल... न्नताभिः रुचिर... वधूभिः परिगततटभूमिः (सम्भेदनः)। जल... न्नताभिः— जलेन निचिडितम् अङ्गलनं यद् वस्त्रं तेन व्यक्ताः निम्नोन्नताः नाभिमध्यकुचमण्डलनितम्बजवनाद्यवयव सन्निवेशाः यासाम् , Whose ups and downs i. e. the depressed and elevated parts of the body are clearly manifested or brought into relief by the garments closely sticking (निबिडित) in water. The picture of sticking ओलेनी, which evoked such hot controversy in the learned circles of Maharashtra, would explain the idea underlined in this expression. Cf. सन्दष्टवत्रेष्ववलानितम्बेषु etc.। रघु XVI. 65. स्नान... त्थिताभिः— स्नानमात्रादुत्थिताभिः— Who have just emerged (from water) after their bath. मात्रपदेन स्नानार्द्रवस्त्रा परित्यागः सूचितः। Com. रुचिर... स्वस्तिकाभिः—- इचिरः यः कनककुम्भः तस्य श्रीः विद्यते अस्य सः, एतादृशः आभोगः (परिपूर्णता) ययोः तौ च तुङ्गौ च कुचौ तयोः विनिहितौ हस्तौ एव स्वस्तिकौ याभिः ताभिः— (By those women) who have placed their hands in a Svastika-like pose i. e. crosswise on their lofty (तुङ्ग) breasts having the fullness of the beauty of bright golden jars. The poet describes the peculiarly natural pose of women under such conditione, and thus betrays a keen sense of observation ! वधूभिः परिगततटभूमिः—The region of whose banks is crowded by young women (वधूभिः).

  The Act is called शार्दूलविभ्रम, as it gives us the incident of the tiger, utilised by the poet mainly to bring मदयन्तिका and मकरन्द together.

**\_\_\_\_\_\_**

 कपालकुण्डला— The name of the female votary of the कापालिक sect. Lit. 'Wearing a human skull as an ear-ornament.'

 V. I. In this verse, कपाल॰ proclaims the glory of शक्तिनाथ, 'the Supreme Divinity' according to the philosophy of her sect. षड...तात्मा— षङ्भिः (चक्रैः) अधिकं यद् दशनाडीचक्रं तत्र स्थितः आत्मा यस्य सः— The Supreme Śiva who resides in (a body in which there are) the six Chakras or Circles and ten Nādis or veins. The six Circles or चक्रऽ are—the ear, the navel, the heart, the throat, the palate, and the intervening space between the eye-brows. Cf. षट्सु कर्णनाभिहृत्कण्ठतालुभ्रूमध्यवर्तिषु शिवशक्तिसंवट्टस्थानेषु नाडीसङ्घट्टेषु हृदाद्यधिष्ठितप्राणविशेषचलनयोगात् चक्रेष्विव। Com. The various gods, forms of the Supreme Being, that reside in these places are these:— नाभौ ब्रह्मा हृदि श्रीशः कण्ठे रुद्रो व्यवस्थितः। ईश्वरो लम्बिकायां च तदूर्ध्वे च सदाशिवः॥ ज्योतिःस्थानानि चैतानि षट्चक्राणि जगुर्बुधाः॥ Bh. दशनाडी— or the Ten Nādis are— इडा. पिङ्गला, सुषुम्णा, सरस्वती, गान्धारी, हस्तिजिह्वा, पूषा, अलम्बुषा, कुहू and शाङ्खिनी. For their places on the body, cf. एताः प्राणवहा ज्ञेयाः प्रधाना दश नाडिकाः। **इडा** नासापुटे वामे **पिङ्गला** दक्षिणे भवेत्। **सुषुम्णा** तालु भित्वैव ब्रह्मद्वारं प्रवर्तिता। **स्वरस्वती** च जिह्वायां **गान्धारी** वामकर्णके। दक्षिणे **हस्तिजिह्वाख्या पूषा** वामे च लोचने। अलम्बुषा दक्षिणे स्याद् गुदद्वारे कुहूर्भवेत्। आञह्मरन्ध्रान्मार्गेण ब्रह्मरन्ध्रस्य **शाङ्खिनी**। सदा बिन्दुवहा ज्ञेया लिङ्गद्वारे च शाङ्खिनी॥ Thus the human body, consisting of seven primary fluids (रसासृङ्मांसमेदोऽस्थिमज्जाशुक्राणि **धातवः**) has six parts or चक्राणि, and ten principal Nādis in a net-work of 72000 veins, whose function is to bear the wind. The whole body is presided over or tenanted by the Supreme Śiva who is deluded by the शक्तिऽ, and especially the प्राणापानमयी शक्ति. Some take षडधिकदशनाडीचक्रं to mean 'a circle of Sixteen Nādis', in which case the following six are added to those already mentioned above, लोलजिह्वा. इभजिह्वा, विजया, कामदा, अमृता and बहुला. हृदि... रूपः— हृदि विनिहितं रूपं यस्य— "Whose form is held within the heart, whose abode is the heart of men.' of ईश्वरः सर्वभूतानां हृद्देशेऽर्जुन तिष्ठति। भ्रामयन् सर्वभूतानि यन्त्रारूढानि मायया॥ भग॰ तद्विदां सिद्धिदः— Who gives miraculous powers to those who know i. e. realise Him. The सिद्धिऽ or Powers are— महिमा लघिमाणुत्वं प्राकाम्यं वशितेशिता। प्राप्तिः कामावसायित्वं शम्भोरैश्वर्यमष्टधा II. अविचलितमनोभिः— With unswerving minds. For the idea in this line, Cf.अन्तर्यश्च मुमुक्षुभिर्नियमितप्राणादिभिर्मृग्यते। विक्र॰ I. 1. शक्तिभिः परिणद्धः— Surrounded or begirt by the 'Powers' or शक्तिऽ. According to the Yoga philosophers, there first existed the Supreme indiscriminate cause of all. Then to the Supreme Being, called शिवः or परः शिवः, a शक्ति called इच्छा was born, and from it sprang क्रियाशक्ति and ज्ञानशक्ति, and from these sprang the god सदाशिव, the representative of the element of ether, from him ईश्वर, the representative of wind, from him रुद्र, the representative of light, from him विष्णु of water, and from him ब्रह्मा of earth. Then followed the rest of the creation.' Bh. The Com. understands eight शक्तिऽ that surround शिव and they are— ब्राह्मी, माहेश्वरी, कौमारी, वैष्णवी, वाराही, माहेन्द्री, चामुण्डा and चण्डिका.

 V. 2. She describes her flight through the sky on the strength of her Yogic miraculous powers, which enable her to be in direct communion with Supreme Śiva and which allow her to go anywhere she likes through the air without the slightest physical exertion. Construe:—नित्यं न्यस्त.. हितं हृत्पद्म... हितं शिवरूपिणम् आत्मानं पश्यन्ती, नाडीनाम् उदयक्रमेण जगतः पञ्चा... कर्षणात् अग्रे नभोऽम्भोमुचः विघटयन्ती (इह) अभ्यागता। नित्यः— Enternal, permanent. Cf.अजो नित्यः शाश्वतोऽयं पुराणो न हन्यते हन्यमाने शरीरे। भग॰ II. न्यस्त... निहितं. 'Fixed or placed by a mystical न्यास or touching, in the circles of the six parts of the body'. न्यास orconsists in repeating a sacred Mantra and touching the six parts of the body (mentioned above) हृत्प... दितं— हृत्पद्मस्य मध्ये उदितम्। शिवरूपिणम् आत्मानं— Atman or the Supreme Spirit, in the form of शिव. लववशात्— Through the power of absorption. 'लय, consequent on समाधि, is a state of mind in which the Yogin is conscious of one thing only, that on which, in a previous process called ध्यन, he has concentrated his mind.' Bh. नाडीनामुदयक्रमेण— पूर्वोक्तानामिडापिङ्गलादीनां वायुपूरणपरिपाट्या। In the course of the swelling of the veins. जगतः पञ्चामृताकर्षणात् शरीरस्य पञ्चभूतात्मकस्य पञ्चामृतानां पृथिव्यप्तेजोवाय्वाकाशानां योगद्धिबलाद्य आकर्षस्तस्मात्— By the drawing off of the five elements from the body (जगतः)—

'When the wind is restrained by प्राणायाम and remains confined in the body, the five elements are drawn off from the body. Ordinarily when the wind moves, the five elements also move and perform their functions; and when it stops, they also stop.' Bh. अप्राप्तोत्पनश्रमा— न प्राप्तः उत्पतनस्य श्रमः यया सा— 'Not subjected to the experience of fatigue in flying up,' as the body becomes as light as cotton. This of course refers to the miraculous powers which a Yogin gets when he has succeeded in the oight processes of the Yoga. They are यम, नियम, आसन, प्राणायाम, प्रत्याहार, धारणा, ध्यान, and समाधि. 'अहिंसासत्यास्तेयब्रह्मचर्यापरिग्रहाः यमाः। पतं॰ यो॰ सू॰ II. 30; शौचसन्तोषतपः स्वाध्यायेश्वरप्रणिधनानि नियमाः। II. 32. स्थिरसुखमासनम्। II. 46. तस्मिन् सति श्वासप्रश्वासयोर्गतिविच्छेदः प्राणायामः। II. 49 स्वविषयासम्प्रयोगे चित्तस्य स्वरूपानुकार सर्वेन्द्रियाणां प्रत्याहार। II. 53. When the mind does not operate on its objects, the other organs of sense, the eye, the ear etc. imitate the mind i. e. cease to perform their functions. This is प्रत्याहार, from whence follows a perfect control over the senses. "देशबन्धश्वित्तस्य धारणा। III. 1. Concentration of the mind on a particular point, the navel, the heart, the head etc., or on any external object. An uninterrupted perception of the object. तत्र प्रत्ययैकतानना ध्यानम्। III. 2. An uninterrupted perception of the object on which the mind is concentrated is ध्यान तदेवार्थ-मात्रनिर्भासं स्वरूपशून्यमित्र समाधिः। III. 3. When the meditator loses his own identity in the thing meditated, the perception of which is the only state of his mind, he is in the state called समाधिः. Then according to the object on which the Yogin, having gone through the previous processes, fixes and concentrates his mind and enters into Samādhi, he acquires miraculous powers of various kinds. The last three processes are called संयम. भुबनज्ञानम् मूर्वे संयमात्। III. 25. चन्द्रे ताराव्यूहज्ञानम्। III. 26 ध्रुवे तद्गतिज्ञानम् III. 27 नाभिचक्रे कायव्यूहज्ञानम्। III. 28. कायाकाशयोः सम्बन्धसंयमाल्लघुतूलसमापत्तश्चाकाशगमनम् III. 41. 'One is able to move in the sky when he becomes light after having performed संयम on such light things as cotton or on the relation of the body to space स्थूलस्वरूप सूक्ष्मान्वयार्थवत्त्वसंयमाद्भूतजयः। त्ततोऽणिमादिप्रादुर्भावः। III, 43-44.'— Bh.

 V. 3. Construe— उल्लोल... णीकः गगन... वेगः मयि पर्याप्तं रमणीयडामरत्वं सन्धते। उल्लो...णीकः— उल्लोलेन यातायातेन स्खलिता या कपालानां कण्ठवर्तिनी माला तस्याः सङ्घट्टेन—क्वणिताः कुरालाः किङ्कण्यः यत्र सः— Where the harsh bells rang in consequence of the garland of skulls striking against them. पर्याप्तं— In an eminent degree,in ample measure.रमणीयडामरत्वं— रमणीयं यद् डामरत्वं भीषणत्वम् उद्भटत्वं वा— Awful grandeur,charming dreadfulness.विघटयन्ती— Clearing all,separating.अम्भोमुच्— A cloud.The word नभम्, as the Com. says, is redundant.

 V. 4. निचि... बद्धः— निविडं यथा तथा ग्रन्थिबद्धः or निबिडेन ग्रन्थिता (by a tight knot) बद्धः। विष्वग्वृत्तिः प्रचलतिविष्वक संर्वतः वृत्तिर्यस्य— Moves about on every side. (विश्वक). खट्वाङ्गघण्टा.— The bell attached to the staff. खट्वाङ्गः— A club or a staff with a skull at the top considered as the weapon of Śiva and carried by ascetics or Yogins.कृतावृत्ति— कृता आवृत्तिः यया सा (घण्टा)— Whirling round and round, moving circuitously. कृतमण्डलभ्रमणा। संस्का... दीर्घ— संस्कारेण सन्तानेन यः काणः तेन दीर्घ— Prolonged by conditions (संस्कारेण) tinkling. पटु रटति— Gives out a sharp sound.विवृ...कुञ्जेषु— विवृतानि यानि निर्मासतया शव शिरांसि तेषां श्रेणयः पङ्क्तयः तासां यानि कुञ्जानि (गहनाः प्रदेशाः) तेषु—In the recesses (कुञ्ज) of the rows of the hollowed (विवृत) human skulls of the corpses. गुञ्जन्—Whistling, howling. अनव... हेतुः— अनवरतः रणत्कारः तस्य हेतुः—रणत्कारः Jingling pealing sound. उत्तालः— Violent पताकाः ऊर्ध्वे धूनोति— flutters my Flags upwards.

 पुराण... गन्धिभिः— पुराणेन निम्बरसेन अक्तं प्रक्षितं परिभुज्यमानं च यद् रसोनं (अम्लरसेनैकेनोनं पञ्चरसं—लसून' इति ख्यातं), तस्य इव गन्धः येषां तैः (धूमः) Stinking like garlic besmeared with old Nimba oil and then fried (परिभृज्यमान. Cf. Mar. भाजणें). The Nimba oil seems to be an extract of the bitter निम्ब fruit. पुरस्ताद् विभावितस्य— To be observed in front.श्मशानवाटस्य— Of the court-yard or the enclosure of the crematorium. पर्य... साधनस्य पर्यवसितं (समाप्तं) मन्त्रसाधनं यस्य तस्य।सविशेष— adv.'On a grand scale'. पूजासम्भारः— A collection of materials (सम्भार) for worship. This is worship in celebration of the successful conclusion of his मन्त्रसाधन which he had commenced with a promise to the deity of a human offering when he has attained the cherished powers by his Sādhana.

उपयाचितं— 'Promised' ; a promise is given to the Deity by the Votary, of a gift in exchange for the reward or successful accomplishment of his desires; it is equivalent to the idea of a 'नवम in Marathi. Cf. यद्दीयते तु देवेभ्यो मतेराज्यस्य सिद्धये। उपयाचितकं' तत्तु देहदं सम्प्रचक्षते॥ हारावली quoted by Com. स्रीरत्नं— A gem of womanhood, the most beautiful woman. विदितं— Known, or obtained (उपलब्धं) उत्त... कुन्तलः— उत्ताभिताः (tied up). कुटिलाः (curly) कुन्तलाः यस्य। कृपाणपाणिः— कृपाणः (sword) पाणी (हरते) यस्य सः।

 V. 5. परिघूसरं (अङगं)— Dusty, sombre, pale. लठि...न्यासः— ललितः विकटश्च न्यास यस्य सः— Whose bearing (न्याप्तः— दहन्यासः) is graceful and yet fierce. न्यास is also urderstood in tho sense of पदन्यास. 'Tread of steps' श्रीमान्— Not a part of the compound, but to be taken separately. “Possessed of glory. मृगा... ननः— मृगाइकनिभं चन्द्रसदृशम् आननं यस्य सः। Construe the last two lines thus— यस्य वामः पाणिः प्रका... हसः प्रवि... पङ्कः लल... ङ्गलः विनयं हरति। प्रका... हसः— प्रकाशितं साहसं येन सः। प्रत्रि... पङ्कः—प्रविगलत् असृकूपङ्कं रुधिरकर्दमः यस्मात्— From which mud-like (clotted) blood was dropping down लल... ङ्गलः— ललत् विलमत्) नरजाङ्गलं (नरमांसं) यत्र सः— With (lunp of) human flesh (held) prominently (in it). विनय हरति— Deprives him of gentle appearance (विनय) पणायिता-विक्रेता— Seller.

 V. 6. The advent of night is being described by the poet in bold fancies with a forceful Gaudī style Construe:— व्योम्रः पर्यन्ताः नापि... वलिभिः इव तमोवल्लरीभिः वियन्त। वसुमती प्रान्तवृत्या नूतने पयसि मज्जति इव। त्रियामा प्रारम्भे अपि वनषु वात्या... प्रकाशं निजं नीलिमानं तरुणयति। व्योम्नः पर्यन्ताः— The line of the horizon, lit. the extreme borders of the sky. तापि...चलीभिः तापिच्छानां तमालपुष्पाणां गुच्छावलिभिः— 'With the bunches of Tamāla flowers', which have a blue-dark hue. तमोवल्लरीभिः त्रियन्ते— Are being filled with the creeper-like (बल्लरी) coils of darkness. वसुमती— The earth. प्रान्तवृत्या— परितः पर्यन्तन्देशनिमज्जनक्रमेण— 'In the gradual course of its extreme borders, from its extremities onwards'. The poet fancies that the earth (like a ship foundered) is sinking in the muddy waters. What sinks first is, therefore, the extreme edges (प्रान्त) of the earth and then afterwards, in this order (वृत्ति) would follow the main portion of the earth. नूतने पयसि— In the fresh muddy waters' corresponding with the darkness. वात्या...प्रकाशं वातानां समूहो वात्या, वात्यानां मण्डलाकारवातानां संवेगेन विवर्तनेन विष्वकू सर्वतः वितता विस्तारिता वलयिता वलयाकारा स्फीता गभीरा या धूम्या (धूमसमूहो नीहारो वा) तद्वत् प्रकाशं सदृशं (नीलिमानं)— Appearing like (प्रकाश) dense (स्फीता) mist or fog (धूम्या), diffused widely (वितता) and formed into curly wreaths (वलयिता) by the violence of the hurricane (वात्या). प्रारम्भेऽपि— Just at the beginning of the night, when we do not get so much darkness. Out in the forests (वनेषु), however, it has become very dark. त्रियामा— The night consisting of three watches or Praharas (याम), the first and the last half Prahara being excluded. नीलिमानं तरुणयति— Intensifies or deepens (तरुणयति— makes young and strong) its dark colour (नीलेमन्).

 The Introductory scene or the बिष्कम्भक of this Act announces the dreadful incident of a young beautiful woman (no other than मालती) soon to be offered as an offering to the terrific goddess Karūlā by अघोरघण्ट, providing at the same time for her rescue by who happens to be on the scene as a 'Seller of human flesh.'

 V. 7. Mādhava in his present love-lorn condition loves to imagine in his mind all those scenes of endearing actions of Mālatī which when conjured up in the fondness of his heart fill him with rapture. प्रेमार्द्राः (चेष्टाः)— Imbued with a passionate longing for each other. प्रेमन् is understood by Com. as सम्भोगप्रीति or 'An emotion which draws the two together and fills them with regard and longings for each other's company.' परस्पराश्रयधनं निरूढं भावबन्धनम्। यदेकायत्ततापाधि तत्प्रेमेति निगद्यत। तेनार्द्राः सरसाः आनुकूल्यशालिन्यः। ...यद्यदस्याः प्रियो वक्ति तस्य तस्याशुकारिताम्। योग्यतामार्द्रतामाहुर्मनःकालुष्यनाशिनीम्।' Com. प्रणयस्पृशः— प्रणयं स्पृशन्ति तेनानुरज्यन्ते इति— Touched or tinged with love. प्रणय, distinguished from प्रेमन् which is the 'first passionate longing' is this very feeling deepened or intensified and therefore reaching the stage of 'Love.' उपचारेर्मिथो यूनोर्यद् बाह्याभ्यन्तराभिधैः। प्रेम नीतं प्रकर्ष चेत् स एव प्रणयः स्मृतः। परिचया...दयाः— परिचयात् तस्यैव प्रणयस्य पुनःपुनरवलोकनसम्भाषणस्पर्शादिभिः परिपोषात्...... प्रौढस्रेहात्मकतापत्तौ सत्यां, उद्गाढः कदाचिदप्यनुपरमः रागः चित्तानुरजकस्रेहप्रकर्षः, तस्य उदयः उद्रेकः यासु ताः— Marked with the manifestation of intense attachment (developed) with growing familiarity.' This is the final stage of love, called स्नेह (Cf. परिणते यत्स्नेहसारे स्थितं) or 'an undying affection for the person loved.' चेष्टाः मयि भवेयुः— May these endearing actions be mine; i.e. may I be the object of these several feelings in Mālatī, since it would be such a delight to observe her behaviour under their influence.” Constru:— यासु आशंसापरिकल्पितासु अपि अन्तःकरणस्य क्षणाद् बाह्य... रोधी आनन्द्रसान्द्रः लयः भवति। आशं... तासु— आशंसया परिकल्पितासु— Imagined in the fondness of hope (आशंसा) by me. कथमेतदीयप्रेमाद्रङ्कटाक्षगोचरो भवेयम्, कथममृतमधुरमाकूतगर्भमस्याः प्रणयवचनमाकर्णयेयम्, कथमेतदीयगाढालिङ्गनसुधारससरसि आत्मानं निमज्जयेयमित्यादिप्रकारेण मनोरथमात्रोपस्थापितासु अपि न तु परमार्थतोऽनुभूयमानासु। Com. बाह्य... रोधी— बाह्यकरणानां व्यापारः, तं रोघ्दु‌ं शीलमस्यास्तीदि— Which instantaneously suspends the functioning of all external organs. आनन्दसान्द्रः लयः— लयः विलीनता, तत्प्रायःपिण्डपाथोन्यायेन तन्मयीभावः— Absorption (producing) deep rapture, an ecstacy of deep (सान्द्र) delight. आनन्दैकप्रचुरः प्रत्यगात्मनः इव ब्रह्मणि आनन्दात्मके विलयो मोक्षदशायां तद्वदित्यर्थः।

 V. 8. Continuing in the same strain of mentally relishing the sweet pleasures of her blissful company, he expresses his fond desires for her close embraces. Construe:— अपि (अहं) अति... स्तनं, प्रियया कर्ण... ननं तदङ्गपरिवर्तम् आप्नुयाम। अपि introduces 'a hope or desire; the sense being would that, how I wish' अति... स्तनं— अतिक्रान्ता मुक्ता यया सा— अतिमुक्ता (मुक्ताहारमपास्य तदर्पणादतिक्रमः) मया ग्रथिता या केसरावली बकुलमाला, तस्याः सतताधिवासेन सुभगौ अर्पितौ स्तनौ मदीयोरसि निवेशितौ यस्मिन तं (अङ्गपरिवर्त)— (An embrace) in which her two breasts are placed (on my bosom), being rendered lovely with the constant fragrance of the Bakula garland woven by me and made to supercede (even) the pearl-necklace. Noto V. L. अतिमुक्तकप्रथित— which is interpreted to mean 'that the Bakula garland had some अतिमुक्त flowers also interwoven with the Bakula flowers.' 'It is not proper, however, for the famous, garland had no अतिमुक्त flower in it when woven by Mādhava'. V. L. अविमुक्त 'never set aside ' is also to be noted, though not. so good, as the idea is to be had from सतताधिवास. कर्णजाह.....ननं— कर्णजाहे (मियया) विनिवेशितं स्वकीयम् आननं यत्र— ' (And the embrace) in.which my beloved has kept her face beneath my ear, Lit leaning.upon or touch the root of the ear.' कर्णजाह is a form obtained by the addition of the suffix जाहन् to the word कर्ण, in the sense of मूल 'root)', acc. to the Sūtra तस्य पाकमूले पिल्वादिकर्णादिभ्यः कुणब्जाहचौ। V. 2—24, and explained as कर्णस्य मूलम्। तदङ्गपरिवर्तम्— तस्याः अङ्गैः परिवर्तः or तस्याः अङ्गस्य परिवर्तः— A close embrace which enfolds (me) by her limbs, or au embrace of her whole body'. V. L. तदङ्गपरिवृत्तिं— 'An exchange between her body and mine.' आलिङ्ग नवशात् तदङ्गं मदधी नं मदङ्गं च तदधीनं भवेदित्यर्थः। Another reading that we have from the Com. is तदङ्कपरिवर्ते 'Rolling in her lap' तस्या अङ्के क्रोडे सर्वतो भावेन वर्तनम्। हृदयालिङ्गनामित्यर्थः यद्वा। तदङ्के परिवर्तनम् ऊर्ध्वाधः क्रमेण पुरुषायितमाप्नुयाम्। It cannot be definitely asserted that the poet, a keen advocate of the Kamasutra, does not intend in the अङ्गपरिवर्त the sense of पुरुषायित, which as described by वात्स्यायन closely approaches the poet's description of the 'embrace' also. Cf. सा प्रकीर्यमाणकेशकुसुमाश्वासविच्छिन्नहासिनी वक्त्रसंसगीर्थ स्तनाभ्यामुरः पीडयन्ती पुनः पुनः शिरो नमयन्ती... ललाटे ललाटे निधाय विश्राम्येत्। काम॰ II. 8. दूरे... एतद्— 'This (stage) is too far off, this is too much to expect.'

 V. 9. He means that he would be satisfied even with the sight of her lovely face which gives him the highest bliss. Construe:— यत्र (यस्मिन् मुग्वे) आलोक पथावतारिणि सुखानि सम्भूय इव चेतसि परं भूमानम् आतन्वते, नेत्रोत्सवः च रतिं प्रस्तौति, यद् (च) बालेन्दु... च्चयाद् अत्रचिनैः सारैः इव उत्पादितं, तत् तस्याः मुखम् अनङ्ग... गृहं भूयः अपि पश्येयम्।.

 आलो... तारिणि— आलोकस्य पन्थानम् अवतरति तस्निन्— Coming within the range of eyes, सुखानि सम्भूयेव— All pleasurable sensations combining or collecting to gether as it were परं भूमानम् आतन्वते— Swell into great magnitude (भूमन्); produce the highest bliss नेत्रोत्सवः— The delight of the eyes. It is called अत्सवः because 'it gives birth (उत्सूते) to joy'. उत्सूते हमित्येव उत्सवः परिकीर्तितः। रतिं प्रस्तौति— Commences a fresh course of love; awakens rautual liking. रतिरिच्छा भवेद् यूनोरुभयप्रार्थनात्मिका। Cf. अकृतार्थेऽपि मनसिजे रतिमुभयप्रार्थना कुरुते। शा॰ II. 1. बाले...यात्— बालेन्दोः याः कलाः, तासाम् उच्चयः राशिः तस्मात्— From the pile of the young moon's digits अवचितैः सारैः उत्पादितं— Fashioned or moulded out of the essences culled. अन...गृहं— अनङ्गस्य मङ्गल गृहम्— The auspicious abode of the Love-God.

 यत्सत्यं— To toll you the truth. तत्सन्द... विशेष‌ः— He means 'even the sight of her face for which I seem to be yearning, will not make the slightest (अतिस्वल्पः) difference in my present condition, for even now she is present in my heart, and I have as vivid a knowledge of her as if she were bodily present before me. Seeing her, therefore, is superfluous. I do see her even now, my whole soul being full of her.'

 मम हि सम्प्रति... चैतन्यम्— The whole passage is a specimen of an abstruse style, in imitation of the Nyāya or Vaiśeşika works, and it presupposes for its understanding a thorough knowledge of some of the technical torms of these systems. Knowledge, which is the basis of all dealings amongst men, is according to them two-fold, viz. अनुभव and स्मृति. While अनुभव or Perception means 'a direct cognition of an object as it really is.' स्मृतिः or 'Remembrance' is the knowledge produced by an impression alone (संस्कारमात्र) created by an object of which direct cognition was already obtained before. Cf. संस्कारमात्रजन्यं ज्ञानं स्मृतिः। We see a certain object whose characteristics or attributes of colour, shape etc. produce in our mind certain impressions (technically called संस्कार or भावना) and then later on, when these impressions are revived in our mind even in the absence of that object, we get a recollection of it. स्मृति, thus, has to be distinguished from, प्रत्यमिज्ञा, which is not recollection, but 're-cognition', that is, the repetition of the knowledge of the same object seen or cognised before. माधव in the first act was 'recognised' by मालती when she saw him again in the garden and identified him with the same young man whom she had seen before and whose impressions of his first sight tallied with the impressions of his second sight and therefore could she say on the strength of this प्रत्यमिज्ञ, "This is he who was seen by me already.' In स्मृति, however, as in the case of माधव of this Act, मालती is not present before his eyes, but the impressions formed about her at her previous meetings have been revived in his mind, and thus bring recollection of her to him. It is these impressions or भावनाऽ (also called संस्कारऽ) which require first of all a direct perception of the object before they can give rise either to स्मृति or to प्रत्यभिज्ञा साति...जन्मनः— सातिशयः दृढतरसंस्काराधान सामर्थ्यलक्षणातिशयसहितः यः प्राप्तः उपलम्भः पूर्वानुभवः। (आपातदर्शन हि कदाचिन्न संस्कारमादध्यात्। आहितो वा संस्कारो दार्ढ्याभावान्न स्मृतिं जनयेत्। बुभुत्सापूर्वकं तु सम्पादितः साधीयाननुभवः संस्कारोत्पादनाव्यभिचारी तदुत्पादितश्च संस्कारों वृढत्वादवश्यं स्मृतिं जनयतीति सातिशयेत्युक्तम्।) तेन सम्भावित आत्मनः जन्म येन सः (संस्कारः)—The संस्कार or the impression which has taken its rise from the former close or vivid (सातिशय) perception.' उपलम्भ is the same as अनुभव or direct cognition of the प्रत्यक्ष type. अनवरतप्रबोधात्— 'By the constant awakening of this संस्कार or impression.' प्रतायमानः— 'Being extended or streched out.' तद्वि......प्रवाहः— तद्विसदृशैः मालती विलक्षणविषयैः ज्ञानान्तरैः अतिरस्कृतप्रवृत्तिः। तथा चान्तरा विषयान्तरास्फुरणान्न प्रवाहतिरस्कार इति भावः। Whose flow (i. e. the flow of this stream of the recalled or recollected image of मालती) is not disturbed or obstructed (अतिरस्कृत) by other cognitions dissimilar or at variance. and inconsistent (विसदृश) with it. प्रिय...सन्तानः— The continuous stream (सन्तान) of the production (उत्पत्ति) of the cognition (प्रत्यय) in the form of a recollection (स्मृति) of my beloved'. He means that this recollection of her starts every moment in mind, the impressions being revived by her various things and peculiar charming characteristics associated with her. अन्त...सारूप्यतः— Owing to the resemblance (सारूप्य) of my mental state to her.' My mental state has almost taken the same likeness, and thus the whole soul has assumed Ler form.' चैतन्यं तन्मयम् इव करोति— Makes my soul or my inmost spirit one with her.' आत्मतत्वं मालतीमयं करोति। ...वेदान्तिनः खल्वेवमाहुः— इन्द्रियार्थसन्निकर्षे सति अन्तःकरणं. परिणामिस्वभावं वृत्याकारेण परिणमते। अन्तःकरणावच्छिन्नं च प्रमातृचैतन्यं वृत्तावपि प्रतिफलति।... तथा च प्रकृतेऽपि स्मृतेर्मालत्याकारकारित्वात् तत्प्रतिफलितचैतन्यं विषयचैतन्येन ऐक्यापन्नं विषयाकारेण स्फुरतीति। नन्वेवं तहिं सा मालतीति एवं प्रतीतिः स्यान्न तु तन्मयत्वम्। किन्तु सन्तानपदं पर्यालोचितं त्वया नैरन्तर्येण स्मर्यमाणतत्तांशविगलनेन 'इय' मिति पुरोवर्तित्वप्रत्यक्षे प्रतिभाति। ततोऽपि चिरकालं तथैव भावनया इदन्तयापि प्रविलयात् प्रमातृचैतन्यतादात्म्यापन्नेव प्रतियत इति भावनाया माहात्म्यमेतदेव। एवं हि कामातुरकामिनीसाक्षात्कारः प्रसिद्धः शास्त्रेषु।

 V. 10. He describes by various poetic images, how his whole being is imbued with Mālatī. 'She is as it were absorbed or dissolved (लीना) with me, as salt is dissolved in water'. But then in that case, she would lose her existence and her identity ! Hence the next fancy, 'she is reflected or mirrored (प्रतिबिम्बिता) in me.' The image in a mirror, however, required the presence of the object (बिम्ब), but Mālatī is absent. The idea of the reflection suits not ! She is portrayed or painted (लिखिता) on my heart within'. A lifeless picture is, however, far different from the real Beauty moving about gracefully in flesh and blood. Why, she is as it were carved (उत्कीर्णा) upon the heart by the Love-gol with his chisel of five arrows !' The carved figure, however, occupies only a part of the body and not the whole! She is, inlaid or implanted (प्रत्युप्ता) within the heart as a gem on the setting of the ring. Even then, the inlaid gem could be extracted. Hence the next fancy, that 'she is glued to it (घटिता) as it were by adamantine coment (वज्रलेप)'. The cement application is only on the surface. 'It appears she is dug deep (निखाता) within me ; she is nailed down (कीलिता) in my mind by all the five arrows (विशिवैः) of the Mind-born (चेतोभुवः) God, i. e. god of Love.' The idea of her being secured by nails is too harsh and cruel in the case of delicate Mālatī ! Therefore the last beautiful fancy of the poet, viz. that she is firmly sewn down (स्यता) in me by a net-work of fine threads in the form of the continuous sallies of thought (चिन्ता) about her ! चिन्ता ... स्यूता— चिन्तायाः सन्ततिः, सा एव तन्तु जालं, तेन निचिडं स्थूता। कलकलः—A great noise. This was required to bring him down on the earth from the heights of heaven wherein he was soaring on the wings of romance. प्रग... कायस्य— प्रगल्भमानप्रगल्भमानः (strutting or stalking about) कौणपानां (goblins, demons) निकायः (समूहः) तस्य। 

 V. 11. Construe:— पर्य...स्त्यानम् आभोगभीमं तमः चिताज्योतिषाम् औज्ज्वल्यै परभागतः प्रकटयति। सं... लयः उत्तालाः कट... तयः किल... हलैः सम्मदात् सांराविणं कुर्वते। पर्य...स्त्यानं— पर्यन्ते ज्योतिषां प्रान्तप्रदेशे प्रतिरोधनशीलं मेदुरं (मांसल) चयेन (संवेन) स्त्यानं (पिण्डीभूतं)— Thickened (म्त्यान) by accumulation and (rendered) dense and impenetrable (to light) at the borders. परभागतः प्रकटयति— Displays (the brilliance— औज्ज्वल्यं) at its best or highest. परभागः— Excess, abundance, height. Cf. आभाति लब्धपरभागतयाधरोष्ठे लीलास्मितं सदशनार्चिरिव त्वदीयम्। रघु॰ V. 70. परभागतः वर्णोत्कर्षात्। तमसि सन्निहिते सति तेजसां कान्त्युत्कर्षः स्फुट एव। Com. आभोगभीमं— आभोगेन (extent) भीमं भीषणम्। संस... लयः संसक्ता (अविच्छिन्ना) आकुला (त्वरायुक्ता) च केलिः येषाम्—Absorbed in their tumultous sports. किल... हलैः— किलकिलारूपैः कोलाहलैः— By their confused kila-kila cries Cf. The Marathi word किलबिलाट. सम्मदात्—Through wild joy. कट... प्रभृतयः— कटपूतना नाम पिशाचविशेषाः— A class of goblins or evil spirits and others of such nature. सांराविणं—A tumultous uproar, a loud shout. For the form cf. अभिविधैा भाव इनुण्। III. 3. 44, and अणिनुणः। V. 4. 15. श्मशाननिकेतनाः— श्मशाने निकेतनं येषाम् —Having their dwelling place in the cemetery.

 V. 12. अशस्त्रपूतं—Not sanctified by weapon. Flesh cut wtih weapons is not desired by goblins, as it is to be had in plenty on the battle-field and moreover it is too pure for the goblins' consumption ! सम्मुखपतितस्य स्वर्गिणो मांसं शस्त्रपूतम्। अतस्तेषामिदमग्राह्यमिदमिति। यद्वा... शस्त्रहतमांसस्य रणे सुलभतया तेषामस्पृहातः इदमतादृशमिति। अव्याजं— निष्कपटं Unadulterated, pure (human flesh), with no fraud in it. genuine. पुरुषा... पकल्पितं— पुरुषस्य अङ्गाद् (आनीय) उपकल्पितं— 'Obtained from male bodies.' Woman's flesh is not relished by the goblins. Cf. अशस्त्रसञ्छिन्नमयोषिदीयं नृमांसमाद्रं गलदस्रबिन्दु यत्। etc. Com. समु... कुलःकुलः— समुच्चलत् उत्तालं यद् वेतालकुलं, तेन मुक्तः तुमुलः अव्यक्तः कलकलः, तेन आकुलः। उत्तालं— Frightful. आकुलः Filled with. प्रचलितः— Moved, set in motion.

 V. 13. Construe:— कर्णा... ग्निभिः दंष्ट्रा ... कटैः इत इतो धाषद्भिः विद्यु... जालैः लक्ष्या... वपुषाम् उल्कामुखानां मुखैः नभः आकीर्यते। उल्कामुखानां— उल्का ज्वाला मुखे येषां ते— Goblins emitting flames of fire through the mouth. The Com. understands thom to be a variety of jackals (शृगालभेदाः) कर्णा... ग्निभिः— कर्णयोः अभ्यर्ण अन्तिकं यावद् विदीर्णाभ्यां सृक्काभ्यां विकटं यद् व्यादानं (आस्यविकासः) तेन दीप्तः अमिर्येषु—In which the fire is blazing at their opening (व्यादान) fierce-looking with its corners (मृक्क) stretched apto the ears. दंष्ट्रा ... कटैः— दंष्ट्राणां (ऊर्ध्वाधः स्थितानां) अप्रैः विसङ्कटैः (विकरालैः)— Dreadful on account of the pointed grinders. आकीर्यते— Is overspread or overcast विद्यु... जालैः— विद्युत्पुञ्जनिकाशानि (तुल्यानि) केशनयनभ्रूश्मश्रुजालानि येषु। विद्युत्पुञ्जः— Mass or cluster of lightning flash. निकाश—

Like, resembling. लक्ष्या... वपुषाम्— (उल्काप्रकाशात्) लक्ष्याणि अन्यदा अलक्ष्याणि विशुष्काणि दीर्घाणि वपूंषि येषाम्— Whose long and shrivelled (विशुष्क) bodies are at one time visible and the next moment invisible (अलक्ष्य) .

 V. 14. पूननचक्रम्— पिशाचविशेषणां चक्रम्— A crowd of goblins. अक्रम... मुक्तै— अक्रमेण अतितृष्णया यौगपद्येन एकीकृत्य कृतः यो ग्रासः कवलपिण्डः, तस्मादर्धमुक्तैः (०विधसैः). Half dropped down from morsels eaten at random (अक्रमेण) . नूमांसविचसैः— नृमांसस्य विवसैः भुक्तशेषैः उच्छिष्टैः—The portions of human flesh left off(uneaten) वृकान् उत्पुष्णन्— Feeding the wolves. आघर्थरं क्रन्दतः(वृकान्)— Howling hoarsely. खर्जूर... जङ्घ— खर्जूरद्रुमदघ्ना(तत्प्रमाणा) जङ्घा यस्य तत्— With their legs measuring (in height) the date palm trees. असित... कङ्काल— असिता श्यामा या त्वक् चर्म, तया नद्राः परीताः विष्वक सर्वतः तताः व्याप्ताः स्नायुग्रन्थयः ताभिः घनानि अस्थिपञ्जराणि यस्य तादृक् च जरतः कङ्कालाः शरीरास्थीनि यस्य तत् तादृक्क च। With gaunt or rotten (जरतः) skeletons whose bony frameworks (अस्थिपञ्जर) are firmly fastened by knots of sinews spread on every side (विष्वक्तत) and covered by black skin.

 V. 15. Construe:— तत... ग्रम् आस्यगर्त विदार्थ विशी... देहा. चल... टराणां दग्ध.. णानाम् इह स्रुतिं दधति। The Pisacas with their wide mouths and a lolling tongue inside are here compared to the old sandal trees having big hollows with pythons wriggling within. पृथु....ग्रं पृथ्वी(broad) चला च रसना(tongue) , तया उग्रं(आस्यगर्तम्)। आस्यगर्त—A mouth-pit, or a cave like mouth. गर्तः— तै— A pit, cave, hollow. विदार्य. Having opened up वित्र... देहाः विवर्णाः शुष्काः च देहाः येषाम्। V. L. विशीर्ण॰. चल... टराणां चलद्भिः अजगरैः घोराणि (भीषणानि) कोटराणि (hollows) येषां (०रोहिणानाम्)। दग्ध... णानाम्— दुग्धाश्च पुराणाश्च रोहिणाः चन्दनाः। Old and burnt sandal trees. 'रोहिणश्चन्दनद्रुमः' इति विश्वः। This stanza contains an instance of the Alaṅkāra called निदर्शना. एते पिशाचा दग्धपुराणरोहिणानां द्युतिं दधतीत्यसम्भवि। अतो रोहिणद्युतिसदृशी तेषां द्युतिरित्युपम्प्रयां पर्यवसानम्।.' Bh. बीभत्सं—Loathsome, nauseous, revolting.

 V. 16. The post seems to revel in describing disgusting scenes of the goblins eating the carrion of the corpses lying about in the cemetery. कृत्तिम् उत्कृत्य. Tearing of the skin (कृत्ति) (of the dead bodies) पृथु ... भूयांसि पृथुना उच्छोफेन भूयांसि (मांसानि) — Increased in bulk (भूयांसि) by great swelling (उच्छोफ). अंस...सुलभानि— अंसषोः स्फिजोः (जघनाभोगमोः) पृष्ठे पिण्डयोः जन्धापाश्वात्यभागयोः च अवयवेषु सुलभानि— To be easily obtained from such parts as the shoulders, hips (स्फिच्), the back and the calf of the leg. (पिण्ड). उग्रपूतीनि— उत्कटगन्धानि— उप्रा पूतिः येषां तानि—Giving out & horrid stink. जग्ध्वा Absolutive form from the rt. अद् 'to eat'— 'Having eaten', आत्त... नेत्रः—आत्तानि (गृहीतानि) स्नायबः अन्त्राणि (intestines) नेत्राणि च येन। V. L. आर्तः पर्यस्तनेत्रः— 'Yelling and looking wildly round about'. प्रकटितदशनः— Showing his teeth. प्रेतरङ्कः— अतिदीनः पिशाचविशेषः—A halfstarved spirit. करङ्कः— The skull; also a skeleton of bones. अङ्कस्थ— Placed on the lap. स्थपुटगतं क्रव्यं— Raw flesh lying even in the uneven parts. (स्थपुटगतं— निन्मोन्नतविषमस्थानगतं). अस्थिसंस्थं— अस्थिषु यत् सन्तिष्ठति तत्— Sticking to the bones. अव्यग्रम् अत्ति— Eats undisturbed (अव्यग्रं).

 V. 17. Another revolting scene of the goblins is b.ing described with almost a devilish pleasure for the loathsome ! The burning corpses are pulled out from the piles and their flesh and marrow is being eaten by them ! Construe:— एते कुणपभुजः निष्टा... स्भः क्वथ... दसः संसक्तधूमान् अपि प्रेतकायान् भूयसीभ्यः चिताभ्यः कृष्ट्वा, उत्प... मांसं सन्धिनिर्मुक्तम् उभयतः प्रचलत् जङ्घानलकं निष्कुष्य उदायिनीउदायिनीः मज्जधारः आरात् पिबन्ति। निष्टा... स्थः— निष्टापेन (निःशेषेण तापः तेन) सम्यकनापेन स्विद्यन्ति क्षरन्मज्जानि अस्थीनि येषां तान् (प्रेतकायान्)— The bones in which (corpses) become moistened with excessive heat (निष्टाप). The V. L. निष्टापस्विद्यदस्नः is accepted by the Com. as the form अस्थ्नः is grammatically incorrect. But this reading is open to the objection that there could be no blood in the dead bodies. It is not unlikely that the poet may not have remembered the rule when he used the word. If, however, for प्रेतकायान् we accept प्रेतकायात् as the reading (given by some), the difficulty is removed.' Bh. क्वथन... मेदसः— क्वथनेम परिणमत् मेदा येषाम्। क्वथनं— Boiling मेदसू— n. Fat or marrow. संसक्तधूमान् संसक्तः धूमः येषां तान—Enveloped in smoke. कुणपभुजः— शवभक्षकाः Goblins who eat dead bodies (कुणप). उत्प... मांसम् उत्पक्कम् अत एव स्रंसि विगलत् मांसं यस्य तत् (०नलके)— From which the flesh is dropping down having been roasted (उत्पक्वं). उभयतः प्रचलत्— Falling down on both the sides. The Com. connects उभयतः with सन्धिनिर्मुक्तम्— ‘Dis-connected from the joints on both the sides,' referring of course to the muscles of the legs, thighs and arms, उभयतः मूलाप्रभागयोः यो सम्धी ताभ्यां निर्मुक्तम्। आरात्— From near or from a distance ! The word has contradictory senses. आराद्दरसमीपयोः। निष्कृष्य— विगतमांसावरणं कुत्त्रा— Having removed the coating of flesh. V. L. निष्कृष्य— Having pulled out; also निश्चुष्य ‘Having sucked.’ चङ्घानलकं— The leg-bone (Cf. Mar. नळी or नरडी).उदयिनीः मज्जधाराः— The stream of marrow (मज्जा) coming out (उदयिनी). प्रादोषिकः— रात्रिप्रारम्भजः— Belonging to the evening time (प्रदोष). The evening revelry (प्रमोदः).

 V. 18. The fiendish revelries of the female spirits on the cemetery— ground are the theme of the verse in which the poet tries to satisfy their sense of decoration and enjoyment with the materials accessible in these loathsome, surroundings. अन्त्रैः...सराः— कल्पितः रचितः मङ्गलार्थ प्रतिसरः यैः। The word प्रतिसर means ‘a cord or a ribbon worn round the wrist or necs as an amulet. ’ It approaches the idea of a मङ्गलसूत्र worn by married ladies as a symbol of their unwidowed condition. अवैधव्यचिह्नं मङ्गलप्रतिसरो भवति। It may also mean ‘a bracelet, marriage-string' a कङ्कण worn as the same symbol as above. The purpose of а प्रतिसर is here served by the intestines of the dead bodies. स्त्री भूतः— स्त्रीहस्त एव रक्तोत्पलं तेन व्यक्तम् उत्तंसं कर्णभूषणं विभ्रति याः— ‘Who wear conspicuous (व्यक्त) ear-ornaments (उन्तंस) of red lotuses in the form of (dead) women's hands.' They have fallen upon the corpses of women in the cemetery, and have cut off the hands from the bodies, to wear them as ear-decorations ! One wonders to what nauseating length the poet can go in his description of the बीभत्सरस ! पिनह्य— Absolutive from the root अपि + नह्. ‘Having put on or worn.’सहसा— ‘Hastily' ; V. L. शिरसा or शिरसो (पिनाह्य) is better, as it agrees with the women's custom of wearing flower-wreaths on the head. हृत्प….स्रजः— 'The garlands of white lotuses in the form of the hearts (of the dead bodies) .' The heart is supposed to be white in colour हृत्पद्मस्य श्वेतनया पुण्डरीकपदेनोपन्यासः। Comi, शोणि... जुषः— शोणितपङ्कः एव कुङ्कुमं तज्जुषन्ति सेवन्ते इति। Applying saffronmarks (on the forehead) by means of the clotted blood. अस्थि...सुराः (पिवन्ति)— Wines (not actual but) in the form of bonemarrow. कपालचषकैः— With the glasses or cups of skulls. Read पिशाचाङ्गनाः। The drinking bouts in the company of their lordsare held by these females, the skulls serving as cups and the marrow the wines ! The stanza is quoted in the to illustrate the doctrine that two sentiments though represented as independent of each other and not mutually related as principal and subordinate, do not affect the beauty of a composition if one of them: contributes to heighten the other, or both to the development of a third. This is an instance in which the and the बीभत्स contribute to develop a third viz. हास्य.' Bh.

 प्रशा... कारैः— प्रशान्ताः भीषणाः विभीषिकायाः प्रकाराः येषाम्— Whose horrid frightening devices have stopped. निःसत्त्वता— Unsubstantial nature. It may also mean Impotent or cowardly nature.' विचितः— 'Searched, surveyed' Ho says this in a mood of dejection (सनिर्वेदं), because although he wandered through the whole area of the cemetery, he could get no customer to purchase from him this precious commodity of the human flesh.

 V. 19. The river with its banks near the cemetery is what we get in this verse. Construe:— गुञ्ज... भीमैः तटैः अन्तः...रवा पारेश्मशानं सरित्। गुञ्जत् भीमैः— गुञ्जतां कुञ्जकुटीरेषु (लतादिपिहितोदरप्रदेशेषु) स्थितानां कौशिकानां (उलूकानां) याः घटाः, तासां धूत्कारैः संवल्गितः यः कन्दतां फेरवाणां जम्बुकानां चण्डः डात्कृतिः (शब्दविशेषः), तेन भृतः प्राग्भारः (अग्रतटं), तेन भीमैः। Dreadful with their foremost slopes (प्राग्भार) filled with the yelling (डात्कृति) of jackals which is mingled with (संवल्गित) the hooting sounds (घुत्कार) of the flocks (घटा) of owls crying (गुञ्जत्) in their tiny nests (कुटीर) inside the bowers अन्तः... रवा— अन्तः शीणीः ये करङ्काः (कपालानि) तेषां कर्कराः (भग्नावयवाः), तैः पयःसंरोधः, तेन कूलङ्कषः स्त्रोतोनिर्गमः, तेन घोरः घर्घररवः यस्याः यस्याः सा (सरित्)— Giving out a terrific gurgling sound (घर्घररव), as the current dashes against the bank (कूलङ्कष), on account of the obstruction of the stream of the water by the pieces (fallen out) from the rotten (शीर्ण) , skulls (करड्क) inside कूलङ्कष— कूल कषतीति— सा तटसङ्घर्षिणी— Scratching the bank. The form with a मुमागम is obtained according to, Sūtra सर्वकूलाभ्रोकरीषेषु कषः। III. 2. 42. Cf. other forms like सर्वेकषः खलः, सर्वेकषा भगवती भवितव्यतैव। I. अभ्रङ्कषो वायुः, करीषकषा वात्या। परेश्मशानं— श्मशानस्ये पारे पर्यन्ते। Cf. पारे मध्ये षष्ठ्या वा। II. I. 18.

 नरे... करणं— नरेन्द्रचित्तस्य आराधनोपकरणं— The tool or the means of pleasing the king साकूतं—'Feelingly, the word आकूत meaning 'feeling or emotion'.

 V. 20. विकल... तारः— विकला भयोद्विग्ना च या कुररी, तस्याः कूजितवत् स्निग्धो मसृणः तारः च—Soft and high-pitched (तार)like the warbling of the affrighted osprey. Cf. सा मुक्तकण्ठं व्यसनातिभाराच्चक्रन्द विग्ना कुररीव भूयः। रघु॰ XV. 68. अये किं नु खलु मद्विज्ञापनानन्तरं कुररीणामिव आकाशे शब्दः श्रूयते विक्र॰ I. श्रोत्रसंवादमेन्ति— प्रत्यभिज्ञागोचरत्वम् एति— Sounds on the ears (श्रोत्र) as one having similarity or correspondence (संवाद with the voice heard before), comes to be recognised. अन्तर्भिन्न— Tossed within, wavering', also 'pierced within'. विह्वलति— Becomes pained or afflicted.

 V. 21. करुणः— Piteous अनिष्टानां— Of disasters or calamities. हतासि— You are undone or ruined. Cf. वयं तत्त्वान्वेषान्मधुकर हतास्त्वं खलु कृती। शा॰ I. 24. कल्या...पारे— कल्याणस्य साधनमेवैकं शुभं तस्मिन् तदेव व सकलो व्यापारो यस्याः— All of whose activities were intended solely for securing my happiness. जीवन्ती— While yet she is alive. सम्भावये. 'Go upto her, wait upon her, help har'. अपि नाम— 'I hope I shall bo able to help etc.'

 V. 22. साव... स्थिति— सावष्टम्भः यो निशुम्भः (पादघातलक्षणपरिभवः) तस्य सम्भ्रमात् नमतः भूगोलस्य निष्पीडनं, तेन न्यञ्चन् (अवनमन्) कर्परः पृष्ठास्थि यस्य, तादृशस्य कूर्मस्य कम्पेन विगलन्ती ब्रह्माण्डखण्डस्य स्थितिः यस्मिन् तत् (क्रीडितं)— In which the balance of a continent of the universe is lost by the quivering of the back-bone of the tortoise (कूर्म), whose back-bone (कर्पर) bends down (न्यञ्चत्)by the pressure of the earth's globe sinking down (नमत्)under the hurried vigorous (सावष्टम्भ) tread (of the goddess).' The universe has the support of the divine Tortoise, the Second Incarnation of Viṣṇu, the god who looks to the world's maintenance. The pressure of the earth under the heavy tread of the goddess acts on the back— bone of this Tortoise which bends under it and thus disturbs the balance of the whole universe and causes the earthquakes ! अनेन भूकम्प उक्तः। पाता...र्णव— पातालस्य प्रतिमल्लयोः— प्रतिभटयोः अधोभुवनकुहर— सदृशयोः गल्लविवरयोः कपोलसुपिरयोः प्रक्षिप्ताः सप्तार्णवाः यत्र तत्— In which the seven oceans are thrown into the abysmal cavities of the cheeks rivalling with (प्रतिभट) the nether world (in depth).गल्ल means the cheek, especially the part of the cheek near the corners of the mouth' Cf. ताम्बूलभूतगल्लोऽयं मल्लं जल्पति मानुषः। etc. का॰ प्र॰ VII. The word is looked upon as ग्राम्य or vulgar नन्दि...र्द्धि नन्दिता या नीलकण्ठस्य परिषद्, तेन व्यक्ता ऋाद्भिः येन यस्य वा— whose glorious worth is manifested by the fact that it delights the assembly of (tha Gaṇas) of Śiva. क्रीडितं— The sport, the play (of danaing) .

 V. 23. The ताण्डव dance of the Goddess is the theme of this wonderful verse whose metre diction and thoughts are well suited to the wild character of the dance which it describes. It is a stanza in a दण्डक metre, consisting of four lines, each composed ef two नगणऽ (नगण =UUU) followed by sixteen रगणऽ (रगण = —U—) , and thus consisting of 54 letters and belongs to that species of दण्डक which is known by the name of सङ्ग्राम'. Bh. The stage direction indicates that it is being acted on the stage, which means probably that both and कपालकुण्डला were themselves dancing to the accompaniment of the singing of this verse, which marked the swing of the step as it were on every syllable that was uttered with force or accent on it. The scheme of accent on which the step would fall would be something like this:—प्रचलितकरिकृत्तिचञ्चन्नखाघातभिन्नेन्दुनिस्यन्दमानामृतश्चयोनजीवत्कपालावर्लामुक्त चण्डादृहासत्रसद्भूरि-भूतप्रवृत्तस्तुति। etc. प्रच... स्तुति— प्रचलिता या (उत्तरीयभूता) कस्कृित्तिः (गजचर्म तत्पर्यन्तेषु) चञ्चन्तः (चञ्चलाः) ये नखाः, तेषाम् आघातेन भिन्नात् (विदीणात्) इन्दोः निष्यन्दमानस्य अभृतस्य श्च्योतेन (क्षरणेन) जीवतां (लब्धजीवानां) कपालाना (मौलिमाल्यग्रथितामा) आवल्या (पङ्क्त्या) मुक्तैः चण्डाट्टहासैः त्रसद्भयः (विभ्यद्भयः) भूरिभ्यः भूतेभ्यः प्रवृता स्तुतिर्यस्य तत् तादृशम्। Whose praise is commenced by the many eseatures frightened by the horrid boisterous. laughters given out by the rows of the skulls that are revived (brought to life) by the nectar trickling from the moon torn by the strokes of the whirling (चञ्चत्) talons (on the fringes) of the elephant hide swinging (with thy dancing steps) to and fro. Fresh elephant—hide dripping with drops of blood is loved by God Śiva who wears it while dancing this wild dance. Of. नृत्यारम्भे हर पशुपतेरार्द्रनागाजिनेच्छाम्। शान्तोद्वेगः स्तिमितनयनं दृष्टभक्तिर्भवान्या ॥ मेघ॰. I. 36 श्वस... धरम्— श्वसतां (अतिखेदात् फूत्कुनाम् असितभुजङ्गानां (कृष्णसर्पाणां) भोगाः एव अङ्गदप्रन्थयः (केयूरबन्धनानि) तेषां निष्पीडनेन स्फारं फुल्लन्त्यः (विकसन्त्यः) याः फणाः तासां पठित् निर्यतः (निर्गच्छतः) विषज्योतिषः उज्जृम्भणेन उड्डामराणां (भयङ्कराणां) व्यस्तानां (विक्षिप्तानां) विस्तारिणां दोष्णां खण्डेन (सन्धेन) पर्यासिताः (परितो विक्षिप्ताः) क्ष्माधराः यस्मिन्। In which the mountains are scattered by the expanding arms tossed about (व्यस्त) and rendered dreadful (उड्डामर) by the flashing up (उज्जृम्भण) of the poison-flames darting from the broad hoods which at pressure (निष्पीडन) are fully expanded by tho black snakes whose coiling bodies serve like knotted arm-decorations (अङ्गदग्रन्थि). ज्वल... भागं ज्वलता अनलेन पिशङ्गानां नेत्रच्छटानां भारेण भीमं यद् उत्तमाङ्ग (शिरः), तस्य भ्रमिः (भ्रमणं) तेन प्रस्तुता या अलातचक्रस्य क्रिया, तस्यां स्यूताः दिग्भागाः यत्र तत्— In which the quarters are sewn together by the blazing circular movement (भ्रमि) as of a fire— brand (अलात) of the head (उत्तमाङ्ग) fierce with the concentrated (भार) lustre of the eyes appearing tawny (पिशङ्ग) by the fire burning, (within). अलातक्रिया— 'A fire-brand moved in circles, very much similar to the sport of moving a long wooden stick (called in Marathi बोथाटी) with blazing cloth-balls at the end उत्तु ... गणम्. उत्तुङ्गस्य खट्वाङ्गस्य शृङ्गध्वजः, तस्य उद्धृतिभिः (उद्धननैः) विक्षिप्ताः (विशीर्णाः) तारागणाः यत्र तत्— Wherein the clustors of stars are scattered about by the waving of the top-flag of the long staff प्रमु... मनः— प्रमुदितानां कटपूतनानाम् उत्तालानां च तालैः स्फुटत्कर्णा अत एव सम्भ्रान्ता या गौरी तस्याः घनाश्लेषेण (गाढालिङ्गनेन) हृष्यन्मनसः त्र्यम्बकस्य आनन्दोऽत्रास्तीति तत् तादृशम्। Which gives delight to the three-eyed God whose heart exults (हृष्यत्) in the close embrace of Pārvatī who is bewildered and has her ears splitting (स्फुटत्) by the clapping of the hands of the wild बेतालऽ and the delighted goblins. अरिष्ट्यै—अशुभाभाषाय— for our welfare. हृष्ट्यै— For our joy.

 V. 24. न्यस्ता... बसना— न्यस्ते अलक्तकरक्ते माल्यवसने यस्यां सा— Wearing garments and flower-garlands dyed red with the Alaktaka dye.एतद् वध्यचिह्नम् This is looked upon as a sign of the human victim to be given as an offering to the deity. Cárudatta who was being. taken to the gallows had also the red flower— garland and red sandal pigment marks impressed on his body. Cf. मृच्छ॰ X. 3, 5. पाखण्डचण्डालयोः— Heretics and villains. वसुः— Name of कुबेर. It alsorefers to a class of deities that are eight in number. Cf. धरो ध्रुवश्च सोमश्च अहश्वेवानिलोऽनलः । प्रत्यूषश्च प्रभासश्च वसवोऽष्टाविति स्मृताः । अस्तकरुणः (विधिः)— अस्ता करुणा यस्मात् सः Pitiless. प्रक्रमः— A course of action.

 न खलु स... स्मरति— A beautiful sentiment coming from the lips. of Mālatī even under these conditions Cf उपरताप्यनुपरता महासेनपुत्री एवमनुकम्प्यमानार्यपुत्रेण । स्वप्न॰ VI. प्रकोष्ठे— At his elbow, in his arm. प्रतिहतोऽसि— निराकृतोऽसि— Frustrated, foiled कापालिकापंसद— An accursed. or wretched Kāpālika.

 V. 28. प्रलापनिरर्गलं प्रक... स्नेहः— For whom affection was V. manifested in words spoken freely or without restraint. प्रलापे निरर्गलं यथा स्यात्तस्था प्रकटितः निजस्नेहः यस्मिन् सः 'The V. L. त्यक्ताशङ्कः and then प्रताप ० or प्रलापनिरगलः make these adjectives applicable to माधव and then प्रकटितनिजस्नेहः will have to be taken as प्रकटितः निजः स्नेहः येन सः i. e. the sense will be on the occasion of her (Mālatī’s) death. माधव has thrown off all reserve or hesitation, has assumed freedom of speech or is free in his prowess (प्रताप ०) and has shown his affection for मालती '. The last epithet is not decorous as involving boastfulness; as to the first he had no reserve before as is shown by his offering his heart and life to in the fourth Act, and there he was free and unrestrained in his speech also. In fact these adjectives appear appropriate in the case of मालती alone... Bh. प्रतीपविपाकिनः (पाप्मनः)— प्रतीपः विपरीतः विपाकः फलारम्भः यस्य तादृशस्य— Reacting adversely (on him).

 V. 27. त्व... जन्मा— तत्र पाणिपङ्कजस्य परिव्रहेण धन्यं जन्म यस्य सः— Blessed in life by the espousal of your lotus-like hand. भूयासम्— Benedictive, I Sing. of ṛt. भू— 'I may be’. अभि... मानः— अभिनिवेशेन कदर्थ्यमानः— Being oppressed by this strong desire.. काकतालीयं— Accidental coincidence. It is a maxim, called the काकतालीय न्याय of the crow and the palm fruit.' It has its origin in the unexpected and sudden fall of a palm fruit upon the head of a crow (so as to kill it) at the very moment of its sitting on a branch. of that tree; and is used to denote a very unexpected and accidental occurrence, whether welcome or unwelcome. Cf. देवात् काकागमनसमये तालफलप तनसदृशम्। Com.

V. 28. चन्द्रकला आननचरीं—The moon's digit entering the mouth of Rāhu. दैवात् (प्रेयसी) समासाद्य— Having luckily found her, my beloved. दस्योः— From the robber. कृपाण...च्छिन्दतः— Snatching her away out of the range (विषय) of the descent of the sword.. Through fear. This feeling was there on account of Mālatī whom he wants to save before she is killed by the villain अघोरघण्ट. द्रुतं— Melted. चेतः कथं वर्तताम्— 'How must my heart be i. e. what is to happen to my heart under these conflicting emotions. Brahmin urchin. The word has also the sense of a fool, a block-head.'

  V. 29. व्याघ्रा... न्यायेन व्याघ्रेण आघाताय (गृहीतायां) मृग्यां कृपाकुलः यः मृग
तन्न्यायेन– According to the maxim or the analogy of a male deer moved by pity for his doe scented i. e. seized by a tiger." Mādhava following Mālatī in her present danger when seized by walauz satisfies this maxim wherein Mālatī corresponds with the doe in the clutches of the tiger-like. Incidentally he suggests that Mādhava would be not only incapable of giving her any help but would himself be his prey, as would be the male deer as against the tiger हिंसारुचेः– हिंसायां रुचिः यस्य तस्य— Who has an inordinate fondness for killing. प्राण्यु... जुषः प्राणिनाम् उपाहारस्य (साधकैः क्रियमाणस्य) केतनं (कृत्यं) तज्जुषः सेवमानस्य (मे)— Engaged in the religious rite of offering a living victim to the goddess.'
